class\u003d\"toctext\"\u003eJSONObject\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cli class\u003d\"toclevel-2\"\u003e\u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-anchor-small\" href\u003d\"#w_atom\"\u003e\u003cspan class\u003d\"tocnumber\"\u003e11.7\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class\u003d\"toctext\"\u003eatom\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cli class\u003d\"toclevel-2\"\u003e\u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-anchor-small\" href\u003d\"#w_server\"\u003e\u003cspan class\u003d\"tocnumber\"\u003e11.8\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class\u003d\"toctext\"\u003eserver\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cli class\u003d\"toclevel-2\"\u003e\u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-anchor-small\" href\u003d\"#w_webscript\"\u003e\u003cspan class\u003d\"tocnumber\"\u003e11.9\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class\u003d\"toctext\"\u003ewebscript\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003ch1\u003eWhy Web Scripts?\u003c/h1\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eWeb Scripts allow you to:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e Build custom URI-identified and HTTP accessible Content Management Web Services\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e Turn your Alfresco repository into a content management powered HTTP Server\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e Easily access, manage, and cross-link your content via a tailored RESTful API\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cp\u003eYou do not need tooling or Java knowledge. All you need is your favourite text editor or the Alfresco Explorer web client: no compilation, generators, server restarts, or complex installs.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e Background\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eAlfresco Web Scripts (introduced in 2006) brought together the worlds of content repository and the web. There\u0027s a blindingly obvious synergy between the two. Consider the web. It\u0027s one huge single collection of inter-related documents. Physically, the documents are located in many machines, in many data centers across the globe, stored and managed with many types of software. And yet, to the user in their browser it\u0027s one huge collection with easy to click links. This logical simplicity is all due to the underpinnings of the web; HTTP, URIs and HTML (and other types of document e.g. XML). So, what has this to do with ECM repositories. ECM Repositories are containers of documents, important documents that are the heart of Enterprises. However, ECM Repositories have traditionally provided proprietary access points therefore restricting potential use of those documents. This is made worse when ECM Repositories multiply within the Enterprise. Those proprietary access points make it difficult to link documents between repositories. But, wait a minute, users on their home PCs can access the world\u0027s huge collection of documents just using their browser. Why can\u0027t it be that easy within the Enterprise?\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eTraditional ECM Repository interfaces are APIs, a collection of programmer methods for interacting with the Repository.\u0026#160; These APIs are barriers to accessing the documents held within the Repository. You can\u0027t get to the documents unless you have a tool that can speak the API. Documents are often identified by some kind of repository-scoped identifier. This style of interface is broadly known as RPC (remote procedure call). It turns out that RPC is not particularly suited to providing the capabilities of the web where distribution and uniform access of content is key. The web underpinnings of HTTP, URIs and media types follow a style known as REST, which stands for Representational State Transfer. Procedure calls are no longer central. Instead, we have uniquely identified Resources (document, feed, stock price, person) via URIs, representations of those resources (HTML, Atom, JSON) containing links to other resources and a small well-defined uniform interface for access (HTTP GET, POST, PUT \u0026amp; DELETE). So, until ECM Repositories become RESTful, it will be difficult to write applications and services that can access all ECM managed content distributed across the Enterprise. Think back to the web. The very essence of a uniform interface gave birth to Google (a search for the world\u0027s documents), Digg (a rating system for the worlds documents) and Delicious (a bookmarking and categorization system for the worlds documents). Within the Enterprise, content oriented services such as Transformation, Encryption, Workflow, Entitlement and Deployment can flourish with a uniform interface.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWeb Scripts provide RESTful access to content held within your Alfresco Enterprise Content Repository. This allows you to place controls on your enterprise content to manage it, and at the same time, provide uniform access for a wide variety of client applications and services e.g. browser, portal, search engine or custom application. Due to the inherent distributed nature of this interface, all Alfresco Content Repositories within the Enterprise can resemble one logical collection of inter-related documents, just like the web. And as with any other web citizen, you can apply web technologies such as caching, authentication, proxies, negotiation etc. to your repository resources.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWith Web Scripts, you can either build your own RESTful interface using light-weight scripting technologies such as JavaScript and Freemarker, allowing you to arbitrarily map any content in the Repository to resources on the web, or you can use pre-built out-of-the-box Web Scripts that already encapsulate many of the mappings. In fact, CMIS (a proposed standard for ECM web services) is implemented in Alfresco as a series of Web Scripts.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eSince 2006, Web Scripts proved themselves exceedingly useful and have been used in all kinds of solutions:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e Integrating Alfresco with 3rd party systems\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e Providing feeds\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e Developing data services\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e Allowing Alfresco to act as a different kind of repository (eg. ActiveResource)\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e Developing UI services such as portlets\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e Customizing search\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e Acting as a back-end to client tools such as Orbean Forms\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e Office href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Creating_a_New_Kind_of_Web_Script\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eKinds of Web Script\u003c/a\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003ch1\u003eWhat is a Web Script?\u003c/h1\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eA Web Script is simply a service bound to a URI which responds to HTTP methods such as GET, POST, PUT and DELETE.\u0026#160; While using the same underlying code, there are broadly two kinds of Web Scripts.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eData Web Scripts\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eData Web Scripts encapsulate access and modification of content/data held in the repository therefore are provided and exposed only by the Alfresco Repository server. They provide a repository interface for client applications to query, retrieve, update and perform processes typically using document formats such as XML \u0026amp; JSON. Out-of-the-box, Alfresco provides a series of Data Web Scripts e.g. for tagging, activities, site management... \u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003ePresentation Web Scripts\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003ePresentation Web Scripts allow you to build user interfaces such as a dashlet for Alfresco Explorer or Alfresco Share, a portlet for a JSR-168 portal, a UI component within Alfresco SURF, a Web Site or a custom Application. They typically render HTML (and perhaps include browser hosted JavaScript). Unlike Data Web Scripts, Presentation Web Scripts may be hosted in the Alfresco Repository server or in a separate presentation server. When hosted separately, the Presentation Web Scripts interact with Data Web Scripts. Out-of-the-box, Alfresco provides a series of Presentation Web Scripts e.g. Portlets, Office Integration, SURF Components...\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eSee the \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts_FAQ\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eWeb Scripts FAQ\u003c/a\u003e for more information.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eImplementation\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe interface of a Web Script comprises of a URI, HTTP methods, and document types. This is all you need to know if you\u0027re just using a pre-built Web Script. However, if you want build your own RESTful interface, it has been made as simple as possible to construct your own Web Script. You do not need tooling or Java knowledge. All you need is your favourite text editor or Alfresco Explorer: no compilation, generators, server restarts, or complex installs.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eA Web Script implementation consists of the following components (often summarized as MVC):\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e A description document, which describes the URI that will initiate the script. For example, the service is given a short name and description, along with authentication and transactional needs. URI bindings are described as \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fbitworking.org%2Fnews%2FURI_Templates\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eURI templates\u003c/a\u003e.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e An optional \u003cstrong\u003e\u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Creating_a_Controller_Script\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003econtroller script\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e, written in JavaScript, which will do the actual work. For example, the script may query the Alfresco repository to build a set of data items, known as a \u003cstrong\u003emodel\u003c/strong\u003e to render in the response, or for URIs that intend to modify the repository (hopefully, PUT, POST \u0026amp; DELETE method bindings), the script may update the Alfresco repository. The JavaScript has access to all URI arguments, Alfresco services and repository data entry points.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e One or more FreeMarker \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Creating_a_Response_Template\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eresponse templates\u003c/a\u003e, known as \u003cstrong\u003eviews\u003c/strong\u003e (or Representations in REST parlance) that will render output in the correct format for your specific needs. For example, HTML, ATOM, XML, RSS, JSON, CSV, or any combination of these. The URL response is rendered via one of the supplied templates where the chosen template is based on the required response content-type or status outcome. The template has access to all URI arguments, common repository data entry points and any data items built by the optional controller script.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cp\u003eAdvanced implementations may fall-back to Java.\u0026#160; The different components (description doc, controller, and templates) are tied together through a document convention. \u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWeb Scripts are registered and executed by the \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eWeb Scripts Framework\u003c/a\u003e.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch1\u003eAlfresco RESTful API Reference\u003c/h1\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eOut-of-the-box, Alfresco provides several RESTful APIs (built as Web Scripts):\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FRepository_RESTful_API_Reference\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eRepository API Reference\u003c/a\u003e - remote services for interacting with the Alfresco Repository\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e TODO: References to older and future versions of API?\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FOpenSearch\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eOpenSearch\u003c/a\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FCMIS_Web_Scripts_Reference\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eCMIS API Reference\u003c/a\u003e - Content Management Interoperability Services\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F2.1_REST_API%23Package%3A%2Forg%2Falfresco%2Fportlets\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003ePortlets\u003c/a\u003e such as My Inbox, My Checked-Out for hosting in any Portal\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F2.1_REST_API%23Package%3A%2Forg%2Falfresco%2Foffice\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eOffice Integration\u003c/a\u003e for hosting in Microsoft Office\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003ch1\u003eHow Do I Use a Web Script?\u003c/h1\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eThis section focuses on using pre-built Web Scripts. You will need to understand:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e What is a URI\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e How to invoke HTTP methods such GET \u0026amp; POST from your environment of choice\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e Optionally, how to construct or parse XML \u0026amp; JSON if using Data Web Scripts\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cp\u003eBasically, Web scripts are URI \u0026amp; HTTP accessible, so it is a case of putting together the correct HTTP request.\u0026#160; Each Web Script is uniquely identified by its URI, although some Web Scripts may support multiple URIs.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eWhere Can I Use a Web Script?\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eWeb Scripts may be used in a number of environments:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework%23Servlet_Runtime\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eHTTP Client\u003c/a\u003e (e.g. Web Browser, HTTP Client API)\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FSurf_Platform\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eAlfresco SURF\u003c/a\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e Alfresco Explorer web client\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework%23JSR-168_Runtime\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eJSR-168 Portal\u003c/a\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework%23JSF_Runtime\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eJSF Page\u003c/a\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FFacebook\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eFacebook Application\u003c/a\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003ch2\u003eAnatomy of a Web Script URI\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eWeb Script URIs are of the form:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003ehttp[s]://\u0026lt;host\u0026gt;:\u0026lt;port\u0026gt;/[\u0026lt;contextPath\u0026gt;/]/\u0026lt;servicePath\u0026gt;\u003ca class\u003d\"\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/\u0026lt;scriptPath\u0026gt;\"\u003e/\u0026lt;scriptPath\u0026gt;\u003c/a\u003e[?\u0026lt;scriptArgs\u0026gt;]\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eWhere:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003ehost - name or address of server hosting the Web Script\u003cbr/\u003eport - port where Web Script is exposed on server\u003cbr/\u003econtextPath - path where application is deployed to, generally /alfresco\u003cbr/\u003eservicePath - path where Web Script service is mapped to, generally /service\u003cbr/\u003escriptPath - path to Web Script (as defined by Web Script)\u003cbr/\u003escriptArgs - arguments to pass to Web Script\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eSome examples:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003ehttp://localhost:8080/alfresco/service/api/path/Workspace/SpacesStore/Company%20Home/children\u003cbr/\u003ehttp://localhost:8081/share/service/mytasks?priority\u003d1\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eDepending on where a Web Script is invoked, the URI may be absolute or relative.\u0026#160; In some cases Web Scripts may be deployed to the root application which means the \u003ctt\u003econtextPath\u003c/tt\u003e is not required.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003ehttp://localhost:8080/service/api/path/Workspace/SpacesStore/Company%20Home/children\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eSome environments (such as \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FSurf_Platform\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eAlfresco SURF\u003c/a\u003e and the Web Script \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework%23JSR-168_Runtime\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003ePortal Runtime\u003c/a\u003e) only require the script path to identify a Web Script.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e/api/path/Workspace/SpacesStore/Company%20Home/children\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe \u003ctt\u003eservicePath\u003c/tt\u003e is generally mapped to \u003ctt\u003e/service\u003c/tt\u003e. However, the means for \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts%23Authenticating\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eauthenticating\u003c/a\u003e may be controlled via this path.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eListing Available Web Scripts\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eAn index of all registered Web Scripts is available at the following URIs:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003ehttp://\u0026lt;host\u0026gt;:\u0026lt;port\u0026gt;/\u0026lt;contextPath\u0026gt;/\u0026lt;servicePath\u0026gt;/\u003cbr/\u003ehttp://\u0026lt;host\u0026gt;:\u0026lt;port\u0026gt;/\u0026lt;contextPath\u0026gt;/\u0026lt;servicePath\u0026gt;/index\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eExample:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003ehttp://localhost:8080/alfresco/service/index\u003cbr/\u003ehttp://localhost:8081/share/service/index\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eA description of each registered Web Script is provided including its URI(s) for calling the Web Script. Some URIs contain {tokens} - those are also valid URIs - they are expressed as \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts%23URI_Templates\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eURI Templates\u003c/a\u003e allowing for the URI path to be parameterized.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe index provides a view of Web Scripts by:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e Package\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e URI\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e Family\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cp\u003eAlso, if there happens to be an issue with the registration of a Web Script, the index also provides a list of Web Scripts that failed registration.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cem\u003eNote: This index page is itself implemented as a Web Script\u003c/em\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cem\u003eNote: The \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%232.1_REST_API\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eAlfresco RESTful API Reference\u003c/a\u003e pages in this WIKI are just index pages rendered as MediaWIKI markup instead of HTML\u003c/em\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eAuthenticating\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eWeb Scripts may require the caller to be authenticated. Each Web Script dictates its own authentication requirements. If a Web Script requires authenticated access and the call is unauthenticated an appropriate authentication process is initiated. Upon successful authentication the Web Script is invoked.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe style of authentication depends on the environment within which the Web Script is hosted e.g. within a servlet run-time HTTP Auth may be used. Within a portal run-time, the portal may decide.\u0026#160; \u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e Repository Authentication Options\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eWhen Web Scripts are hosted within the Repository server two options are available for authentication.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003col\u003e\u003cli\u003e HTTP BASIC Authentication - the authentication process follows the handshake as defined by \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Ftools.ietf.org%2Fhtml%2Frfc2617\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eRFC2617\u003c/a\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e Alfresco Explorer Authentication - the authentication process supported by the Explorer Web Client, that is the authentication mechanism as defined by the alfresco global properties \u003cem\u003eauthentication.chain\u003c/em\u003e.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ol\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe first is useful for external systems that wish to programmatically invoke Alfresco RESTfully (that is, using standard HTTP mechanisms), whereas the second is useful when single sign on is required across both the Alfresco Explorer Client and the Web Script, such as linking from the Explorer to a Web Script page. \u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe caller can choose which authentication option by specifying an appropriate \u0026lt;servicePath\u0026gt; in the Web Script URI.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003col\u003e\u003cli\u003e /service \u003d\u0026gt; HTTP Basic Authentication e.g. \u003ctt\u003e\u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"http://localhost:8080/\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\"\u003ehttp://localhost:8080/\u003c/a\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eservice\u003c/strong\u003e/api/path/Workspace/SpacesStore/Company%20Home/children\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e /wcservice \u003d\u0026gt; Alfresco Explorer Authentication e.g. \u003ctt\u003e\u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"http://localhost:8080/\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\"\u003ehttp://localhost:8080/\u003c/a\u003e\u003cstrong\u003ewcservice\u003c/strong\u003e/api/path/Workspace/SpacesStore/Company%20Home/children\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ol\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cem\u003eNote: In both cases, the successful authentication may be remembered in the caller session, thus only requiring the authentication process to be initiated once\u003c/em\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e Pre-Authorized Calls\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eTo force authenticated access specify the following URI argument:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003ealf_ticket\u003d\u0026lt;ticket\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor example\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003ehttp://\u0026lt;host\u0026gt;:\u0026lt;port\u0026gt;/\u0026lt;contextPath\u0026gt;/\u0026lt;servicePath\u0026gt;/api/path/Workspace/SpacesStore/Company%20Home/children\u003cstrong\u003e?alf_ticket\u003d\u0026lt;ticket\u0026gt;\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eTickets may be established by the calling environment (e.g. Alfresco SURF) or explicitly using the \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F2.1_REST_API%23Login\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eLogin Web Script APIs\u003c/a\u003e.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e Guest Access\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eWeb scripts may allow guest access.\u0026#160; To force guest access specify the following URL argument:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003eguest\u003dtrue\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor example\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003ehttp://\u0026lt;host\u0026gt;:\u0026lt;port\u0026gt;/\u0026lt;contextPath\u0026gt;/\u0026lt;servicePath\u0026gt;/api/path/Workspace/SpacesStore/Company%20Home\u003cstrong\u003e?guest\u003dtrue\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eContent Negotiation and Response Formats\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eEach Web Script returns its result in a reponse stream. The result may be encoded in one or more formats (i.e. mimetypes) such as HTML, XML or JSON depending on the capabilities of the invoked Web Script.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIf a Web Script call does not provide any hints on which response encoding to use, the Web Script uses its pre-defined default encoding. However, a client can provide the following hints:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003col\u003e\u003cli\u003e URL extension e.g. \u003ctt\u003e\u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"http://\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\"\u003ehttp://\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan\u003e\u0026lt;host\u0026gt;:\u0026lt;port\u0026gt;/\u0026lt;contextPath\u0026gt;/\u0026lt;servicePath\u0026gt;/api/path/Workspace/SpacesStore/Company%20Home/children\u003c/span\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e.atom\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e Format Argument e.g. \u003ctt\u003e\u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"http://\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\"\u003ehttp://\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan\u003e\u0026lt;host\u0026gt;:\u0026lt;port\u0026gt;/\u0026lt;contextPath\u0026gt;/\u0026lt;servicePath\u0026gt;/api/path/Workspace/SpacesStore/Company%20Home/children\u003c/span\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e?format\u003datom\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e Accept Header (as defined by \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwww.w3.org%2FProtocols%2Frfc2616%2Frfc2616-sec14.html\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eHTTP 1.1\u003c/a\u003e)\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ol\u003e\u003cp\u003eHints 1 \u0026amp; 2 specify a Web Script Format which a \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework%23HTTP_Response_Formats\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eregistered short name\u003c/a\u003e for a mimetype. The typical mimetypes are mapped:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003cstrong\u003ehtml\u003c/strong\u003e\u0026#160; \u003d\u0026gt; text/html\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003cstrong\u003etext\u003c/strong\u003e \u003d\u0026gt; text/plain\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003cstrong\u003exml\u003c/strong\u003e\u0026#160; \u003d\u0026gt; text/xml\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003cstrong\u003eatom\u003c/strong\u003e\u0026#160; \u003d\u0026gt; application/atom+xml\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003cstrong\u003erss\u003c/strong\u003e\u0026#160; \u003d\u0026gt; application/rss+xml \u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003cstrong\u003ejson\u003c/strong\u003e\u0026#160; \u003d\u0026gt; application/json\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cp\u003eHint 3 is typically provided by a Web Browser, although may be controlled programmatically via many HTTP client libraries and is specified as a comma-separated of mimetypes and preferences.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cem\u003eNote: Each Web Script dictates which of the above hints are adhered to via its Web Script Description\u003c/em\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eTunneling HTTP Methods\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eNot all clients can issue all HTTP methods. In the most severe case, a client may be restricted to GET and POST only. In this situation, web scripts provide two mechanisms for issuing any HTTP method via POST:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e HTTP Request Header \u0027\u003ctt\u003eX-HTTP-Method-Override\u003c/tt\u003e\u0027\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e URI parameter \u0027\u003ctt\u003ealf_method\u003c/tt\u003e\u0027\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003ci\u003eNote: If both the header and query parameter are specified in the request, the \u003cstrong\u003eheader\u003c/strong\u003e takes precedence over the query parameter.\u003c/i\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIn either case, the value is set to the HTTP method name to be invoked.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor example, if the HTTP DELETE method is not supported by a client, but the client wishes to delete a repository folder, the following may be issued:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003ePOST X-HTTP-Method-Override\u003dDELETE \u003ctt\u003ehttp://\u0026lt;host\u0026gt;:\u0026lt;port\u0026gt;/\u0026lt;contextPath\u0026gt;/\u0026lt;servicePath\u0026gt;/api/path/Workspace/SpacesStore/Company%20Home/\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cpre\u003ePOST \u003ctt\u003ehttp://\u0026lt;host\u0026gt;:\u0026lt;port\u0026gt;/\u0026lt;contextPath\u0026gt;/\u0026lt;servicePath\u0026gt;/api/path/Workspace/SpacesStore/Company%20Home?alf_method\u003dDELETE\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eForcing Success Response Status\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eNot all clients can gracefully handle non-success HTTP Responses, for example, the Flash runtime player - the runtime for Adobe Flex applications.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIn this situation, web scripts provide a mechanism to force all HTTP Responses to indicate success in their Response Header.\u0026#160; However, the Response body will still represent the content as if a non-success status had occurred.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eTo force HTTP Response Header success set the following HTTP Request Header:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e \u003ctt\u003ealf-force-success-response\u003c/tt\u003e \u003d \u003ctt\u003etrue\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eJSON Callbacks\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eIf your web scripts provide JSON responses, it is likely they will be invoked directly from within a Web Browser via the XMLHttpRequest object. However, due to security reasons, you may run into cross-domain issues, a restriction that requires you to proxy your requests on the server side. Typically, to workaround these issues, public services such as \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fdeveloper.yahoo.com%2Fjavascript%2Fjson.html\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eYahoo! JSON Services\u003c/a\u003e provide a callback mechanism.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWeb scripts also provide this mechanism which wraps the JSON output text in parentheses and a function name of your choosing. A callback is invoked by adding the following URL parameter on JSON URL requests:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e alf_callback\u003d\u003ci\u003efunction\u003c/i\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003ewhere \u003ci\u003efunction\u003c/i\u003e is the name of a client-side JavaScript function to be invoked.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe following simple HTML page demonstrates this:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eThis will result in the JSON response looking like this:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003eshowTitle( \u003ci\u003e...json output...\u003c/i\u003e );\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eNOTE:\u003c/strong\u003e For security reasons, this mechanism is disabled by default. To enable it on any SpringWebScripts container, set the bean property: allowCallbacks \u003d true, for example:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;bean id\u003d\u0027webscripts.container\u0027 parent\u003d\u0027webscripts.abstractcontainer\u0027 class\u003d\u0027org.springframework.extensions.webscripts.PresentationContainer\u0027\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u0026lt;property name\u003d\u0027name\u0027\u0026gt;\u0026lt;value\u0026gt;Spring Web Scripts Container\u0026lt;/value\u0026gt;\u0026lt;/property\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u0026lt;property name\u003d\u0027allowCallbacks\u0027\u0026gt;\u0026lt;value\u0026gt;true\u0026lt;/value\u0026gt;\u0026lt;/property\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160; ...\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;/bean\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eCaching\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eWeb Scripts comply with \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwww.w3.org%2FProtocols%2Frfc2616%2Frfc2616-sec13.html\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eHTTP Caching\u003c/a\u003e supporting the notions of Last Modified Time and ETag allowing a Web Script response to be cached. A cache manager (suitable for the client environment) can interpret the cache controls (if any) returned with the Web Script response and cache appropriately.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eA typical scenario is where a Repository-hosted Web Script is invoked via HTTP. In this case, any HTTP caching proxy may be used between the client and Alfresco Repository Server.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cem\u003eNote: Each Web Script dictates its caching controls, if any\u003c/em\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch1\u003eHow Do I Create a Web Script?\u003c/h1\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eThis section demonstrates how to create a Web Script. The Web Script in question is a simple Hello World example requiring authenticated access which simply greets the user in both HTML and XML.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eYou will need to understand:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e XML for expressing the Web Script description\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e Optionally, JavaScript for writing Web Script behaviour\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e Freemarker for rendering a Web Script response\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe only tools you\u0027ll need are an Alfresco Repository server and the Alfresco Explorer web client. Alternatively, advanced Web Scripts may be \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Java-Backed_Implementations\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003edeveloped in Java\u003c/a\u003e.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eExamples and Guidelines\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eBefore diving into the technical bit, you may want to browse or refer to the available \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts_Examples\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eWeb Scripts Examples\u003c/a\u003e.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIf you\u0027re really impatient, you can create your \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003ehelloworld.get.properties\u003c/a\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eThese files need to be stored in a folder somewhere. They can live in either the Alfresco Repository or the Java ClassPath.\u0026#160; The following folders are listed in the sequence in which Alfresco searches for Web Script implementation files:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003col\u003e\u003cli\u003e repository folder: \u003ccode\u003e/Company Home/Data Dictionary/Web Scripts Extensions\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e repository folder: \u003ccode\u003e/Company Home/Data Dictionary/Web Scripts\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e class path folder: \u003ccode\u003e/alfresco/extension/templates/webscripts\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e class path folder: \u003ccode\u003e/alfresco/templates/webscripts\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ol\u003e\u003cp\u003eWithin any of these folders, you can use subfolders to organize web scripts.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eNew web scripts will not be visible until the \u0027Refresh Web Scripts\u0027 link is clicked on the /alfresco/service/ page.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eWarning!\u003c/strong\u003e do not store web scripts in:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e/org/alfresco\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eor any of its subfolders - these folders are reserved for Alfresco use.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eCreating a Description Document\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eOur URI is described by creating an .xml description document in one of the above Web Script folders. For now, assume all files are placed into the repository folder: \u003ctt\u003e/Company Home/Data Dictionary/Web Scripts\u003c/tt\u003e.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWithin any Web Script folder, sub-folders may be used to organise Web Scripts. For example, we can place our Hello World Web Script in the folder\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e/Company Home/Data Dictionary/Web Scripts/org/alfresco/sample\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eand within this folder, create the file\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003ehelloworld.get.desc.xml\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eNaming is important. Web Scripts employ convention over configuration for their definition to reduce the amount of required typing. The postfix \u003ctt\u003e.desc.xml\u003c/tt\u003e informs Alfresco that this is a Web Script description document.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe complete folder and file name\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eorg/alfresco/sample/helloworld\u003c/strong\u003e.\u003cstrong\u003eget\u003c/strong\u003e.desc.xml\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003edefines\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003col\u003e\u003cli\u003e A package of \u003cstrong\u003eorg/alfresco/sample\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e A service id of \u003cstrong\u003ehelloworld\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e A binding to the HTTP \u003cstrong\u003eGET\u003c/strong\u003e method\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ol\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cbr/\u003eThe content of the Hello World Web Script description document is defined as follows:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u0026lt;webscript\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;shortname\u0026gt;Hello World\u0026lt;/shortname\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;description\u0026gt;Greet a user\u0026lt;/description\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;url\u0026gt;/helloworld?to\u003d{name?}\u0026lt;/url\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;url\u0026gt;/hello/world?to\u003d{name?}\u0026lt;/url\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;format default\u003d\u0027html\u0027\u0026gt;extension\u0026lt;/format\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;authentication\u0026gt;user\u0026lt;/authentication\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026lt;/webscript\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eWhere:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003eshortname\u003c/tt\u003e is a human readable name for the Web Script\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003edescription\u003c/tt\u003e (optional) is documentation for the Web Script\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003eurl\u003c/tt\u003e (one or more) is a \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts%23URI_Templates\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eURI Template\u003c/a\u003e to which the Web Script is bound; variants of the URI template which specify a format do not need to be registered, however, they are useful for documentation purposes\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003eformat\u003c/tt\u003e (optional) controls how the content-type of the response can be specified via the URI; valid values are:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003eargument\u003c/tt\u003e the content-type is specified via the \u003ctt\u003eformat\u003c/tt\u003e query string parameter, for example \u003ctt\u003e/helloworld?to\u003ddave\u0026amp;\u003cstrong\u003eformat\u003dxml\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003eextension\u003c/tt\u003e the content-type is specified via the URI extension, for example \u003ctt\u003e/hello/world\u003cstrong\u003e.xml\u003c/strong\u003e?to\u003ddave\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003eany\u003c/tt\u003e either of the above can be used\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e Note: if not specified, the default value is \u003ctt\u003eany\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e Note: if the caller does not specify a required content-type at all, the default content-type is taken from the (optional) \u003ctt\u003edefault\u003c/tt\u003e attribute of the \u003ctt\u003eformat\u003c/tt\u003e element. By default, if not set, the html format is assumed. In some cases, a URI may decide upon a response content-type at runtime. For these URIs, specify an empty format, for example \u003ctt\u003eformat default\u003d\u0027\u0027\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003eauthentication\u003c/tt\u003e (optional) is the required level of authentication; valid values are:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003enone\u003c/tt\u003e specifies that no authentication is required at all\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003eguest\u003c/tt\u003e specifies that at least guest authentication is required\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003euser\u003c/tt\u003e specifies that at least named user authentication is required\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003eadmin\u003c/tt\u003e specifies that at least a named admin authentication is required\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e Note: if not specified, the default value is \u003ctt\u003enone\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e Note: The optional runas attribute can be used to force the execution of a web script as a specific user. This can only be specified for web scripts that are stored in the Java Class path.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe description provides Alfresco with all the necessary information to bind the web script to one or more URIs.\u0026#160; It also provides enough to document the Web Script.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eAdvanced Description Options\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eDescription documents also provide the following options, which are important, but not as frequently used or mandated.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003etransaction\u003c/tt\u003e (optional) is the required level transaction; valid values are:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003enone\u003c/tt\u003e specifies that no transaction is required at all\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003erequired\u003c/tt\u003e specifies that a transaction is required (and will inherit an existing transaction, if open)\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003erequiresnew\u003c/tt\u003e specifies that a new transaction is required\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e Note: If not specified, the default value is \u003ctt\u003enone\u003c/tt\u003e if \u003ctt\u003eauthentication\u003c/tt\u003e is also \u003ctt\u003enone\u003c/tt\u003e, otherwise the value is \u003ctt\u003erequired\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003efamily\u003c/tt\u003e (optional) is a tag for categorizing similar or related web scripts. The family tag may be repeated if this script belongs to more than one family.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003ecache\u003c/tt\u003e (optional) is the required level of caching; valid child elements are:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003enever\u003c/tt\u003e (optional) specifies whether caching should be applied at all; valid values (optional) are:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003etrue\u003c/tt\u003e (default) specifies the web script response should never be cached\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003efalse\u003c/tt\u003e specifies the web script response may be cached\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e Note: If \u003ctt\u003enever\u003c/tt\u003e is not specified, the default is \u003ctt\u003etrue\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003epublic\u003c/tt\u003e (optional) specifies whether authenticated responses should be cached in a public cache; valid values (optional) are:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003etrue\u003c/tt\u003e (default) specifies the web script authenticated response may be cached in a public cache\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003efalse\u003c/tt\u003e specifies the web script authenticated response may not be cached in a public cache\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e Note: If \u003ctt\u003epublic\u003c/tt\u003e is not specified, the default is \u003ctt\u003efalse\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003emustrevalidate\u003c/tt\u003e (optional) specifies whether a cache must revalidate its version of the web script response in order to ensure freshness; valid values (optional) are:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003etrue\u003c/tt\u003e (default) specifies that validation must occur\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003efalse\u003c/tt\u003e specifies that validation may occur\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e Note: If \u003ctt\u003emustrevalidate\u003c/tt\u003e is not specified, the default is \u003ctt\u003etrue\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003enegotiate\u003c/tt\u003e (zero or more) associates an Accept header MIME type to a specific web script format of response; the (mandatory) value specifies the format while the mandatory \u003ctt\u003eaccept\u003c/tt\u003e attribute specifies the MIME type\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e Note: Content Negotiation is enabled with the definition of at least one \u003ctt\u003enegotiate\u003c/tt\u003e element\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003ekind\u003c/tt\u003e (optional) is an attribute discriminator for overriding the \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Creating_a_New_Kind_of_Web_Script\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003ekind of web script\u003c/a\u003e. See list of \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Kinds\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eavailable web script kinds\u003c/a\u003e.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003elifecycle\u003c/tt\u003e (optional) is an attribute for describing the \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Script_Lifecycle_\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003elifecycle\u003c/a\u003e of the web script. Web scripts typically start out in some sort of draft state, are promoted to full production use, and are then retired at the end of their life.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003enone\u003c/tt\u003eThis web script is not part of a lifecycle.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003esample\u003c/tt\u003e This web script is a sample and is not intended for production use.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003edraft\u003c/tt\u003e This method may be incomplete, experimental, or still subject to change.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003epublic_api\u003c/tt\u003e This method is part of the Alfresco public API and should be stable and well tested.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003edraft_public_api\u003c/tt\u003e This method is intended to eventually become part of the public API but is incomplete or still subject to change.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003edeprecated\u003c/tt\u003e This method should be avoided. It may be removed in future versions of Alfresco.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003einternal\u003c/tt\u003e This script is for Alfresco use only. This script should not be relied upon between versions. It is likely to change.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cp\u003eAn example of a full web script description follows:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u0026lt;webscript \u003cstrong\u003ekind\u003d\u0027org.alfresco.httpsonly\u0027\u003c/strong\u003e\u0026gt; \u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;shortname\u0026gt;Hello World\u0026lt;/shortname\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;description\u0026gt;Greet a user\u0026lt;/description\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;url\u0026gt;/sample/helloworld?to\u003d{name}\u0026lt;/url\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;url\u0026gt;/sample/helloworld.xml?to\u003d{name}\u0026lt;/url\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;format default\u003d\u0027html\u0027\u0026gt;extension\u0026lt;/format\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;lifecycle\u0026gt;sample\u0026lt;/lifecycle\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;authentication \u003cstrong\u003erunas\u003d\u0027fred\u0027\u003c/strong\u003e\u0026gt;user\u0026lt;/authentication\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u003cstrong\u003e\u0026lt;transaction\u0026gt;required\u0026lt;/transaction\u0026gt;\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u003cstrong\u003e\u0026lt;family\u0026gt;Sample\u0026lt;/family\u0026gt;\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u003cstrong\u003e\u0026lt;cache\u0026gt;\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u003cstrong\u003e\u0026lt;never\u0026gt;false\u0026lt;/never\u0026gt;\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u003cstrong\u003e\u0026lt;public\u0026gt;false\u0026lt;/public\u0026gt;\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u003cstrong\u003e\u0026lt;mustrevalidate/\u0026gt;\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u003cstrong\u003e\u0026lt;/cache\u0026gt;\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u003cstrong\u003e\u0026lt;negotiate accept\u003d\u0027text/html\u0027\u0026gt;html\u0026lt;/negotiate\u0026gt;\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u003cstrong\u003e\u0026lt;negotiate accept\u003d\u0027text/xml\u0027\u0026gt;xml\u0026lt;/negotiate\u0026gt;\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026lt;/webscript\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eURI Templates\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eA URI template is simply a URI containing tokens which may be substituted with actual values. The URI template \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fjcp.org%2Fen%2Fjsr%2Fdetail%3Fid%3D311\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003esyntax\u003c/a\u003e is minimal and simple, and as of Alfresco v3, complies with the template syntax of JSR-311 (JAX-RS). Common forms of URI template include:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003ccode\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e/content/a/b/c/d.txt\u003cbr/\u003e/sample/helloworld?to\u003d{name?}\u003cbr/\u003e/blog/search?q\u003d{searchTerm}\u0026amp;amp;n\u003d{numResults}\u003cbr/\u003e/people/{personName}/profile/{profileStyle}\u003cbr/\u003e/blog/category/{category}?n\u003d{itemsperpage?}\u003cbr/\u003e/user/{userid}\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eA token of the form {\u0026lt;name\u0026gt;?} means it is optional. Typically, tokens are used for URI arguments, but may also be used for path segments.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eNote the third example passes two parameters to the Web Script. Normally an ampersand (\u0026amp;) is used to separate parameters, though in your XML Web Script Description document one must use the escaped literal \u0027\u0026amp;amp;\u0027 instead.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor now, Web Scripts do not enforce mandatory arguments. However, it is still useful to provide a full URI template for documentation purposes.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eURI templates are specified relative to \u003ctt\u003e\u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"http://\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\"\u003ehttp://\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan\u003e\u0026lt;host\u0026gt;:\u0026lt;port\u0026gt;/\u0026lt;contextPath\u0026gt;/\u0026lt;servicePath\u0026gt;\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/tt\u003e.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWhen a URI request is made, Alfresco locates the appropriate Web Script by finding the closest match to a URI template in a Web Script description document. \u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eGiven the following URI Templates:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e1 \u003ctt\u003e/a\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e2 \u003ctt\u003e/a/b\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e3 \u003ctt\u003e/a/{val1}\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e4 \u003ctt\u003e/a/{val1}/b\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e5 \u003ctt\u003e/a/{val1}/b/{val1}\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e6 \u003ctt\u003e/a/{val1}/b/{val2}\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe following URIs match the above templates as follows:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e/a \u003d\u0026gt; template 1\u003cbr/\u003e/a/b \u003d\u0026gt; template 2\u003cbr/\u003e/a/c \u003d\u0026gt; template 3\u003cbr/\u003e/a/b/b \u003d\u0026gt; template 4\u003cbr/\u003e/a/c/b \u003d\u0026gt; template 4\u003cbr/\u003e/a/c/b/c \u003d\u0026gt; template 5\u003cbr/\u003e/a/c/b/d \u003d\u0026gt; template 6\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eHowever, the following URIs do not match any of the above templates:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e/b\u003cbr/\u003e/a/c/c\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eAs an implementor of a Web Script you have access to the values provided for tokens in the URI template e.g. access to the values for \u003ctt\u003e{val1}\u003c/tt\u003e and \u003ctt\u003e{val2}\u003c/tt\u003e. The values are available in both the Web Script \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Creating_a_Controller_Script\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eController Script\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Creating_a_Response_Template\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eResponse Templates\u003c/a\u003e via the root object \u003ctt\u003e\u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23url\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eurl.templateArgs\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/tt\u003e.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cbr/\u003eWhen using java backed controllers the tokens can be accessed through the \u003ccode\u003eorg.alfresco.web.scripts.WebScriptRequest.getServiceMatch()\u003c/code\u003e API. In Community Edition 3.2r2 this will return a \u003ccode\u003eorg.alfresco.web.scripts.Match\u003c/code\u003e instance that has a \u003ccode\u003egetTemplateVars()\u003c/code\u003e method returning a Map of all tokens.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eCreating a Controller Script\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eA Web Script may optionally execute some JavaScript on invocation of its respective URI. The JavaScript can perform queries or updates against a back-end store. Also, the JavaScript may build a data model that is passed to the appropriate Web Script response template for subsequent response rendering.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor our example Hello World service we create the following file in the same folder as the Web Script description document\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003ehelloworld.get.js\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eAgain, naming conventions apply where controller script file names have the following structure\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u0026lt;serviceId\u0026gt;.\u0026lt;httpMethod\u0026gt;.js\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe following JavaScript root objects are available to all Web Scripts, regardless of their hosting environment.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e args: an associative array of all URI parameters. See \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts_Examples%23URL_Argument_Handling\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eexample\u003c/a\u003e.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e argsM: an associative array of all URI parameters (where each key is an argument name and each value is an array containing all respective argument values, even if only one is supplied). See \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts_Examples%23URL_Argument_Handling\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eexample\u003c/a\u003e.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e headers: an associative array of all request headers.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e headersM: an associative array of all request headers (where each key is an header name and each value is an array containing all respective header values, even if only one is supplied). See \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts_Examples%23URL_Argument_Handling\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eexample\u003c/a\u003e.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23url\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eurl\u003c/a\u003e: provides access to the URI (or parts of the URI) that triggered the web script.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e model: An empty associative array which may be populated by the JavaScript. Values placed into this array are available as root objects in Web Script response templates.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23status\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003estatus\u003c/a\u003e: provides ability to control response status codes.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23cache\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003ecache\u003c/a\u003e: provides ability to control caching of response.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Web_Script_Configuration\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003econfig\u003c/a\u003e: provides access to the Web Script configuration.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e msg: provides access to Web Script localized messages.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23format\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eformat\u003c/a\u003e: provides information on the response format to be rendered.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e guest: A boolean indicating whether the web script is executing as \u0027Guest\u0027.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003ewebscript\u003c/a\u003e: An associative array of meta-data properties describing the Web target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003ejsonUtils\u003c/a\u003e: A host object for parsing and generating JSON objects.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e See the \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FJavaScript_API%23Logging_API\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eLogging API\u003c/a\u003e. \u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eWeb Scripts hosted within the Alfresco Repository tier also have access to the following root objects which provide direct access to Repository services and content.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e roothome: the repository root node (only available if authenticated)\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e companyhome: the company home folder (only available if authenticated)\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e person: the person node of the currently authenticated user (only available if authenticated)\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e userhome: the user home folder (only available if authenticated)\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e search: A host object providing access to Lucene and Saved Search results. Web Script response templates rendered after the execution of the JavaScript will now also have the root object named \u003ctt\u003ewho\u003c/tt\u003e, which in this case represents the name of the person to greet.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eOf course, a Web Script can also perform updates, in which case, the \u003ctt\u003emodel\u003c/tt\u003e root object can be used to record items that have been updated, status, and so on.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eDebugging a Controller Script\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe Alfresco Server provides a built-in \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FJavaScript_API%23Alfresco_Javascript_Debugger\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eJavascript debugger\u003c/a\u003e.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eCreating a Response Template\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe final stage of a Web Script is to render a response for the HTTP request. Multiple response formats may be provided. Responses are rendered by FreeMarker templates.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor our example Hello World service, we create the following file in the same folder as the Web Script description document\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003ehelloworld.get.html.ftl\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eAgain, naming conventions apply where response template file names have the following structure\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u0026lt;serviceId\u0026gt;.\u0026lt;httpMethod\u0026gt;.\u0026lt;format\u0026gt;.ftl\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003ewhere\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e \u003ctt\u003eformat\u003c/tt\u003e specifies the format of the response template whose value is one of the following \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts_Framework%23HTTP_Response_Formats\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eformats\u003c/a\u003e.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe following FreeMarker template root objects are available to all Web Scripts, regardless of their hosting environment. \u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e args: an associative array of all URI parameters. See \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts_Examples%23URL_Argument_Handling\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eexample\u003c/a\u003e.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e argsM: an associative array of all URI parameters (where each key is an argument name and each value is an array containing all argument values, even if only one is supplied). See \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts_Examples%23URL_Argument_Handling\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eexample\u003c/a\u003e.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e headers: an associative array of all request headers.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e headersM: an associative array of all request headers (where each key is an header name and each value is an array containing all respective header values, even if only one is supplied). provides access to the URI (or parts of the URI) that triggered the web script.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e \u003ca Script.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" provides information on the response format to be rendered.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e guest: A boolean indicating whether the web script is executing as \u0027Guest\u0027.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\"
