An associative array of meta-data properties describing the server hosting the Web Script.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e date: A date representing the date and time of the web script request.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eWeb Scripts hosted within the Alfresco Repository tier also have access to the following template root objects which provide direct access to Repository services and content.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e roothome: the repository root node (only available if authenticated)\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e companyhome: the company home folder (only available if authenticated)\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e person: the person node of the currently authenticated user (only available if authenticated)\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e userhome: the user home folder (only available if authenticated)\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eWeb Scripts hosted within the presentation tier (i.e. within Alfresco SURF) have their own extras as described in the \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FSurf_Platform_-_Freemarker_Template_and_JavaScript_API\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eSurf Platform - Freemarker Template and JavaScript API\u003c/a\u003e. \u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAnd remember, the FreeMarker template also has access to any root objects created by the controller script, if one has been associated with the Web Script.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWeb script templates also have access to the following methods:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e absurl(url): Returns an absolute URL representation of the passed url. Useful when rendering links within ATOM (and similar formats).\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e xmldate(date): Returns an ISO8601 formatted result of the passed date. Useful when rendering dates within XML.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e scripturl(queryString): Returns a url that references this web script. The passed \u003ctt\u003equeryString\u003c/tt\u003e is added to the url. System arguments such as \u003ctt\u003eguest\u003c/tt\u003e and \u003ctt\u003eformat\u003c/tt\u003e are automatically added. Note, this method is particularly useful for protection against the runtime environment within which the web script is executing. In some environments (such as a Portal) the url may be encoded.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e clienturlfunction(funcName): Generates a client-side JavaScript function that can generate a URL back to this web script.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e argreplace(argString, argName, argValue, ...): Replace specified argName with argValue, or add argName if it does not exist in argString.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e encodeuri(uriString): encode string into URL-safe form.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor our example blog search, we can write the following FreeMarker to render the HTML response:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160; At ${date?datetime}, ${person.properties.userName} says hello to ${toWho?html}\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u003cbr/\u003e \u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eNote how the above template makes use of standard root objects, for example \u003cstrong\u003e${date?datetime}\u003c/strong\u003e and root objects created by the controller script, for example \u003cstrong\u003e${toWho?html}\u003c/strong\u003e.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eMultiple Response Formats\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eMultiple response formats are simply supported by creating further template files following the naming convention outlined above.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cem\u003eNote: New and updated Templates are automatically registered and will be honoured when the Web Script is next invoked.\u003c/em\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor our Hello World example, we can support add a machine-readable XML response by adding the following file\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003ehelloworld.get.xml.ftl\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003ewhose content is\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u0026lt;helloworld\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;from\u0026gt;${person.properties.userName}\u0026lt;/from\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;says\u0026gt;hello\u0026lt;/says\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;to\u0026gt;${toWho?xml}\u0026lt;/to\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026lt;/helloworld\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eWith our Hello World example description document and associated templates, the following URI mappings are available:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e HTML template: \u003ctt\u003e/\u0026lt;contextPath\u0026gt;/\u0026lt;servicePath\u0026gt;/sample/helloworld?to\u003dfriend\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e HTML template: \u003ctt\u003e/\u0026lt;contextPath\u0026gt;/\u0026lt;servicePath\u0026gt;/sample/helloworld?to\u003dfriend\u0026amp;format\u003dhtml\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e HTML template: \u003ctt\u003e/\u0026lt;contextPath\u0026gt;/\u0026lt;servicePath\u0026gt;/sample/helloworld.html?to\u003dfriend\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e XML template: \u003ctt\u003e/\u0026lt;contextPath\u0026gt;/\u0026lt;servicePath\u0026gt;/sample/helloworld?to\u003dfriend\u0026amp;format\u003dxml\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e XML template: \u003ctt\u003e/\u0026lt;contextPath\u0026gt;/\u0026lt;servicePath\u0026gt;/sample/helloworld.xml?to\u003dfriend\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eResponse Status\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eWeb Scripts use HTTP response status codes to:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cul\u003e\u003cli\u003e inform a client of an error situation (for example, item not found)\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e inform a client of an occurrence of an event (for example, item created)\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e instruct a client to perform a follow-up request (for example, authorization required)\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003cli\u003e inform a client of success\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003cp\u003eResponse status codes are set in the controller script via the \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23status\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003estatus\u003c/a\u003e root object.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWe can add a status to our Hello World example indicating that we can only greet one person at a time i.e. the \u0027to\u0027 argument is specified only once. We can use status code 400 (Bad Request) to represent this. The controller script is extended as follows:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eif (argsM.to\u0026#160;!\u003d null \u0026amp;\u0026amp; argsM.to.length \u0026gt; 1)\u003cbr/\u003e{\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160; status.code \u003d 400;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160; status.message \u003d \u0027Can only greet one person at a time.\u0027;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160; status.redirect \u003d true;\u003cbr/\u003e}\u003cbr/\u003eelse\u003cbr/\u003e{\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160; model.toWho \u003d (args.to\u0026#160;!\u003d null)\u0026#160;? args.to\u0026#160;: person.properties.userName; \u003cbr/\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e}\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eRedirect allows the rendering of a custom response template for the specified status code. If redirect is not set (that is, false), the response header status code is set but the relevant standard web script response template is used, as would normally apply.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eIf redirect is true, then an appropriate status response template is searched for. The search is performed in the following order:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e Web Script specific template named \u003ctt\u003e\u0026lt;scriptid\u0026gt;.\u0026lt;method\u0026gt;.\u0026lt;format\u0026gt;.\u0026lt;code\u0026gt;.ftl\u003c/tt\u003e\u0026#160;: located in the same folder as the web script description document and used for the specified status code only, for example \u003cbr/\u003e \u003ctt\u003e/org/alfresco/sample/helloworld.get.html.400.ftl\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e Web Script specific template named \u003ctt\u003e\u0026lt;scriptid\u0026gt;.\u0026lt;method\u0026gt;.\u0026lt;format\u0026gt;.status.ftl\u003c/tt\u003e\u0026#160;: located in the same folder as the web script description document used for any status code, for example\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003ctt\u003e/org/alfresco/sample/helloworld.get.html.status.ftl\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e Package level template named \u003ctt\u003e\u0026lt;format\u0026gt;.\u0026lt;code\u0026gt;.ftl\u003c/tt\u003e\u0026#160;: this template is first located in the package of the web script, but if not found, is searched for in the parent package hierarchy, up to the root package, for example \u003cbr/\u003e \u003ctt\u003e/org/alfresco/sample/html.400.ftl\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e Package level template named \u003ctt\u003e\u0026lt;format\u0026gt;.status.ftl\u003c/tt\u003e\u0026#160;: this template is first located in the package of the web script, but if not found, is searched for in the parent package hierarchy, up to the root package, for example \u003cbr/\u003e \u003ctt\u003e/org/alfresco/sample/html.status.ftl\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e Default template named \u003ctt\u003e\u0026lt;code\u0026gt;.ftl\u003c/tt\u003e\u0026#160;: located in the root package and always renders html, for example \u003cbr/\u003e \u003ctt\u003e/400.ftl\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e Default template named \u003ctt\u003estatus.ftl\u003c/tt\u003e\u0026#160;: located in the root package (provided out-of-the-box) and always renders html, for example \u003cbr/\u003e \u003ctt\u003e/status.ftl\u003c/tt\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eStatus Response templates have access to the same root objects as standard Web Script response templates. The exception is that the default templates \u003ctt\u003e/\u0026lt;code\u0026gt;.ftl\u003c/tt\u003e and \u003ctt\u003e/status.ftl\u003c/tt\u003e only have access to the root objects \u0027\u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23url\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eurl\u003c/a\u003e\u0027, \u0027\u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23status\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003estatus\u003c/a\u003e\u0027, \u0027\u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23server\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eserver\u003c/a\u003e\u0027 and \u0027date\u0027.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eTo provide a custom Bad Request status response for our Hello World example we create the following file in the same folder as the web script description document\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003ehelloworld.get.html.400.ftl\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003ewhose content is\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160; ${status.message}\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u003cbr/\u003e \u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eWe can also provide a meaningful response for machine-readable XML requests:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003ehelloworld.get.atom.400.ftl\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u0026lt;response\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;code\u0026gt;${status.code}\u0026lt;/code\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;codeName\u0026gt;${status.codeName}\u0026lt;/codeName\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;codeDescription\u0026gt;${status.codeDescription}\u0026lt;/codeDescription\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;message\u0026gt;${status.message}\u0026lt;/message\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026lt;/response\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eRemember, these templates are optional, as the search for an appropriate status template will always eventually find the default template \u003ctt\u003e/status.ftl\u003c/tt\u003e.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch1\u003eAdvanced Implementations\u003c/h1\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eConfiguration\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eConfiguration is accessed via the \u003ctt\u003econfig\u003c/tt\u003e root object, which is available during both controller script and template execution.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThere are 3 types of configuration, \u0027script\u0027, \u0027scoped\u0027 and \u0027global\u0027. Script configuration is defined in an XML document with an arbitary structure stored locally with the Web Script. Global and scoped configuration are specified in Alfresco configuration files, as used in Alfresco Explorer.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch3\u003eWeb Script Configuration\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eWeb Script configuration is read from an XML file packaged with the Web Script.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor our example Hello World service we create the following file in the same folder as the Web Script description document\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003ehelloworld.get.config.xml\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eAgain, naming conventions apply where configuration file names have the following structure\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u0026lt;serviceId\u0026gt;.\u0026lt;httpMethod\u0026gt;.config.xml\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe content of the configuration may be any valid XML.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u0026lt;helloworld\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;greeting\u0026gt;hello\u0026lt;/greeting\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;fromproperty\u0026gt;userName\u0026lt;/fromproperty\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026lt;/helloworld\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan\u003eWithin a Controller Script, access to the configuration is via E4X which is essentially \u0027ECMAScript For XML\u0027 (tutorials can be found at \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"http://www.w3schools.com/xml/xml_e4x.asp\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\"\u003ehttp://www.w3schools.com/xml/xml_e4x.asp\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan\u003e and/or \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"http://wso2.org/library/1050\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\"\u003ehttp://wso2.org/library/1050\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan\u003e, \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"http://phpforms.net/tutorial/tutorial.html\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\"\u003ehttp://phpforms.net/tutorial/tutorial.html\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan\u003e).\u003c/span\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eWe can update our Hello World Controller script example to determine how to display \u0027who\u0027 the greeting is from.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003emodel.toWho \u003d (args.to\u0026#160;!\u003d null)\u0026#160;? args.to\u0026#160;: person.properties.userName;\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cstrong\u003evar s \u003d new XML(config.script);\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cbr/\u003emodel.fromWho \u003d person.properties[\u003cstrong\u003es.fromproperty\u003c/strong\u003e]; \u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eFreeMarker has \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwww.freemarker.org%2Fdocs%2Fxgui.html\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003ebuiltin support for processing XML data\u003c/a\u003e allowing response templates direct access to configuration too. We can update our Hello World template example to extract the greeting from the configuration.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160; At ${date?datetime}, ${fromWho?html} says ${\u0027\u0027\u0027config.script.helloworld.greeting\u0027\u0027\u0027?html} to ${toWho?html}\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u003cbr/\u003e \u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch3\u003eGlobal and Scoped Config\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eGlobal and scoped config is read by the Alfresco \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FConfig_Service\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eConfiguration Service\u003c/a\u003e. padding: 0px;\"\u003e\u0026#160;\u003c/p\u003e\u003c/dd\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eConfiguration sections that do not have an evaluator or condition are known as \u0027global\u0027 config sections i.e. these will always appear in a configuration lookup, a typical global configuration section has the following appearance.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u0026lt;alfresco-config\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;config\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u0026lt;server\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u0026lt;errorpage\u0026gt;/jsp/error.jsp\u0026lt;/errorpage\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u0026lt;loginpage\u0026gt;/jsp/login.jsp\u0026lt;/loginpage\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u0026lt;guesthome enabled\u003d\u0027true\u0027\u0026gt;/jsp/guesthome.jsp\u0026lt;/guesthome\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u0026lt;url\u0026gt;/\u0026lt;/url\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u0026lt;url\u0026gt;/alf\u0026lt;/url\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u0026lt;url\u0026gt;/alfresco\u0026lt;/url\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u0026lt;/server\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;/config\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026lt;/alfresco-config\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eScoped configuration, on the other hand, is a configuration section that does have an evaluator and condition, for example.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u0026lt;alfresco-config\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;config evaluator\u003d\u0027string-compare\u0027 condition\u003d\u0027Remote\u0027\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u0026lt;remote\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u0026lt;endpoint\u0026gt;http://localhost:8080/alfresco\u0026lt;/endpoint\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u0026lt;/remote\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160; \u0026lt;/config\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026lt;/alfresco-config\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor changes in these files to take effect, the ALFRESCO server must be stopped and restarted (refreshing the webscripts is not sufficient).\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch3\u003eAccessing Global and Scoped Configuration\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eAccessing the configuration above is achieved using the same techniques and syntax as any other model data, the global configuration is exposed via the \u003ctt\u003econfig.global\u003c/tt\u003e root object and the scoped config is exposed via the \u003ctt\u003econfig.scoped\u003c/tt\u003e root object.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eFor example to access the server configuration from the example above the following syntax would be used in a JavaScript:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003evar serverCfg \u003d config.global.server;\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eand the following syntax would be used in a FreeMarker template:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u0026lt;serviceId\u0026gt;.\u0026lt;httpMethod\u0026gt;.properties\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eEach line of the file represents a message identified by a unique key. The key may be dot separated.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eOur example consists of:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003eat\u003dAt\u003cbr/\u003esays\u003dsays\u003cbr/\u003eto\u003dto\u003cbr/\u003egreeting.hello\u003dhello\u003cbr/\u003egreeting.howdy\u003dhowdy\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eMessages are accessed via the template method \u003ctt\u003emsg\u003c/tt\u003e.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe Hello World HTML template is updated as follows:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160;\u0026#160; ${msg(\u0027at\u0027)} ${date?datetime}, ${fromWho?html} ${msg(\u0027says\u0027)} ${msg(\u0027greeting.\u0027 + config.script.helloworld.greeting)} ${msg(\u0027to\u0027)} ${toWho?html}\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160; \u003cbr/\u003e \u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eMulti-part Form Processing\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eWhen posting a request of mimetype \u003ctt\u003emultipart/form-data\u003c/tt\u003e the following additional root object is available to the Controller Script.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23formdata\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eformdata\u003c/a\u003e: provides access to multipart/form-data requests allowing the upload of files.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eThis root object allows a Web Script to read all fields included in the form including those of type \u0027file\u0027. It provides a mechanism for iterating through each field and examining its meta-data such as name, value, content type etc.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eAll fields that are not of type \u0027file\u0027 are also mapped into the \u003ctt\u003eargs\u003c/tt\u003e and \u003ctt\u003eargsM\u003c/tt\u003e root objects allowing access to fields by name.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eView the \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts_Examples%23File_Upload\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eFile Upload Example\u003c/a\u003e to see how \u003ctt\u003eformdata\u003c/tt\u003e is used to upload files into the Alfresco Repository. \u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eRequest Processing\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eA Controller Script can gain access to a request body allowing the processing of content posted to a Web Script.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eBy default, the following root object is provided:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e requestbody: a \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eScriptContent\u003c/a\u003e representing the content of the request body\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eAs with throws IOException;\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eJava Helper Classes\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eAbstract helper classes are also provided to simplify the This kind of Web Script supports all the behaviour described in this document, with the addition of first executing some Java. As with the controller script, the Java code can build a data model that is available to Response templates. The Java to be executed is placed into the \u003ctt\u003eexecuteImpl\u003c/tt\u003e method.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eManaging Response Status\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eA Java implemented web script also has support for response status codes. There are two approaches to sending a response code:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e Approach 1 - Throw an Exception\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eAll exceptions thrown from a Web Script are caught by the Web Script Runtime and converted to response status codes. By default, the status code 500 (Internal Error) is used. However, the exception \u003ctt\u003eWebScriptException\u003c/tt\u003e supports the constructor:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003epublic WebScriptException(int statusCode, String message)\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eThis constructor is used to explicitly set a response code in an error situation, for example\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003eif (req.getParameter(\u0027q\u0027) \u003d\u003d null || req.getParameter(\u0027q\u0027).length() \u003d\u003d 0)\u003cbr/\u003e{ \u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160; message, as well as control the redirect to a status response template, for example\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003eif (req.getParameter(\u0027q\u0027) \u003d\u003d null || req.getParameter(\u0027q\u0027).length() \u003d\u003d 0)\u003cbr/\u003e{\u003cbr/\u003e\u0026#160;\u0026#160; status.setRedirect(true);\u003cbr/\u003e}\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eCreating a New Kind of Web Script\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eBy default, Alfresco Web Scripts support an \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework%23Web_Script_MVC\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eMVC style\u003c/a\u003e of implementation. Sometimes, it\u0027s useful to override the default behavior to add an extra capability, or provide a completely different style of Web Script such as those that need to stream large amounts of data back on the response. This can be done by developing a Java-backed implementation, however, it cannot be re-used across several Web Scripts without changes to Spring configuration.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eA Web Script \u0027Kind\u0027 allows a Java-backed implementation to be named, and for any Web Script Description Document to state it wants to use that implementation instead of the out-of-the-box one provided by Alfresco. See list of currently available \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Kinds\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eWeb Script kinds\u003c/a\u003e.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe steps for creating a new \u0027Kind\u0027 are:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e Implement a Web Script backing bean\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe steps here are exactly the same as for any other Java-backed implementation as described above.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e (optional) Implement a Description Document Extension\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe backing bean may be configured via extensions to the Web Script Description Document. To access those extensions it is necessary to provide an implementation of the interface:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003eorg.alfresco.web.scripts.DescriptionExtension\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003ewhich defines the following method:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e/**\u003cbr/\u003e * Gets the custom description extensions\u003cbr/\u003e * \u003cbr/\u003e * @param serviceDescPath\u0026#160; path to service doc\u003cbr/\u003e * @param serviceDesc\u0026#160; service doc input stream\u003cbr/\u003e * @return\u0026#160; extensions mapped by name\u003cbr/\u003e */\u003cbr/\u003epublic Map\u0026lt;String, Serializable\u0026gt; parseExtensions(String serviceDescPath, InputStream servicedesc);\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe method parses the complete Description Document (XML), extracts its extensions and places them into a map (indexed by the name of extension) which is returned. It is called when the Web Script is registered with the Web Script framework.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eSpring is used to register the Description Extension implementation:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u0026lt;bean id\u003d\u0027\u003cstrong\u003ewebscriptdesc\u003c/strong\u003e.my.kind.of.web.script\u0027 class\u003d\u0027my.kind.of.WebScriptDocumentExtension\u0027/\u0026gt;\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe id is the same as the Web Script backing bean except it starts with \u003ctt\u003ewebscriptdesc\u003c/tt\u003e instead of \u003ctt\u003ewebscript\u003c/tt\u003e.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e (optional) Access Extensions within your Web Script Implementation\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eTo gain access to your extension values within your backing bean you can use the following method which returns the map created above:\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cpre\u003egetDescription().getExtensions()\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eThat\u0027s it. To use your new \u0027Kind\u0027 of Web Script refer to \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Advanced_Description_Options\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eAdvanced Description Options\u003c/a\u003e. Note: The id referenced in the \u003ctt\u003ekind\u003c/tt\u003e attribute is specified without the \u003ctt\u003ewebscript.\u003c/tt\u003e prefix.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch1\u003eHow Do I Administer Web Scripts?\u003c/h1\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003eResetting the Web Script Index\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eNew and updated Web Scripts can be registered without restarting the Alfresco server. This makes it easy to use the Alfresco Repository to develop Web Scripts.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cp\u003eTo register a Web \u003d\u0026gt; fred\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ul\u003e\u003ch3\u003eURL and authentication\u003c/h3\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eYou can reuse the web clients authentication by using Change the URL to /alfresco/service/ and you will get an HTTP authentication prompt even if you are logged in in the Alfresco web client. The first option is the most convenient for the end user, the second may be useful while testing with different accounts.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003estatus\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eAn associative array of response status properties that allow control over the status and content of the Web Script response.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cdl\u003e\u003cdt\u003e code: (read/write) status code (primarily a HTTP status code, but can be any number)\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003cdt\u003e codeName: (read) human readable status code name\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003cdt\u003e codeDescription: (read) human readable status code description\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003cdt\u003e message: (read/write) status message\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003cdt\u003e redirect: (read/write) a boolean indicating whether to redirect to a status specific response template\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003cdt\u003e exception: (read/write) the exception (if any) which has caused this status\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003cdt\u003e location: (read/write) the absolute URI to which the client should resubmit a request - often used with 3xx redirect status codes.\u0026#160; See \u003ca class\u003d\"jive-link-external-small\" href\u003d\"https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url\u003dhttp%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts_Examples%233xx_Status_Code_Redirection\" rel\u003d\"nofollow\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eexample\u003c/a\u003e.\u003cbr/\u003e\u003c/dt\u003e\u003c/dl\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003ch2\u003ecache\u003c/h2\u003e\u003cbr/\u003e\u003cp\u003eAn associative array of cache control properties that allow control over how the Web Script response is cached.          <h1>Why Web Scripts?</h1>
         <br>
         <p>Web Scripts allow you to:<br></p>
         <br>
         <ul>
          <li> Build custom URI-identified and HTTP accessible Content Management Web Services<br></li>
          <li> Turn your Alfresco repository into a content management powered HTTP Server<br></li>
          <li> Easily access, manage, and cross-link your content via a tailored RESTful API<br></li>
         </ul>
         <p>You do not need tooling or Java knowledge. All you need is your favourite text editor or the Alfresco Explorer web client: no compilation, generators, server restarts, or complex installs.<br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            Background
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <p>Alfresco Web Scripts (introduced in 2006) brought together the worlds of content repository and the web. There's a blindingly obvious synergy between the two. Consider the web. It's one huge single collection of inter-related documents. Physically, the documents are located in many machines, in many data centers across the globe, stored and managed with many types of software. And yet, to the user in their browser it's one huge collection with easy to click links. This logical simplicity is all due to the underpinnings of the web; HTTP, URIs and HTML (and other types of document e.g. XML). So, what has this to do with ECM repositories. ECM Repositories are containers of documents, important documents that are the heart of Enterprises. However, ECM Repositories have traditionally provided proprietary access points therefore restricting potential use of those documents. This is made worse when ECM Repositories multiply within the Enterprise. Those proprietary access points make it difficult to link documents between repositories. But, wait a minute, users on their home PCs can access the world's huge collection of documents just using their browser. Why can't it be that easy within the Enterprise?&nbsp;&nbsp; <br></p>
         <p>Traditional ECM Repository interfaces are APIs, a collection of programmer methods for interacting with the Repository.&nbsp; These APIs are barriers to accessing the documents held within the Repository. You can't get to the documents unless you have a tool that can speak the API. Documents are often identified by some kind of repository-scoped identifier. This style of interface is broadly known as RPC (remote procedure call). It turns out that RPC is not particularly suited to providing the capabilities of the web where distribution and uniform access of content is key. The web underpinnings of HTTP, URIs and media types follow a style known as REST, which stands for Representational State Transfer. Procedure calls are no longer central. Instead, we have uniquely identified Resources (document, feed, stock price, person) via URIs, representations of those resources (HTML, Atom, JSON) containing links to other resources and a small well-defined uniform interface for access (HTTP GET, POST, PUT &amp; DELETE). So, until ECM Repositories become RESTful, it will be difficult to write applications and services that can access all ECM managed content distributed across the Enterprise. Think back to the web. The very essence of a uniform interface gave birth to Google (a search for the world's documents), Digg (a rating system for the worlds documents) and Delicious (a bookmarking and categorization system for the worlds documents). Within the Enterprise, content oriented services such as Transformation, Encryption, Workflow, Entitlement and Deployment can flourish with a uniform interface.<br></p>
         <p>Web Scripts provide RESTful access to content held within your Alfresco Enterprise Content Repository. This allows you to place controls on your enterprise content to manage it, and at the same time, provide uniform access for a wide variety of client applications and services e.g. browser, portal, search engine or custom application. Due to the inherent distributed nature of this interface, all Alfresco Content Repositories within the Enterprise can resemble one logical collection of inter-related documents, just like the web. And as with any other web citizen, you can apply web technologies such as caching, authentication, proxies, negotiation etc. to your repository resources.<br></p>
         <p>With Web Scripts, you can either build your own RESTful interface using light-weight scripting technologies such as JavaScript and Freemarker, allowing you to arbitrarily map any content in the Repository to resources on the web, or you can use pre-built out-of-the-box Web Scripts that already encapsulate many of the mappings. In fact, CMIS (a proposed standard for ECM web services) is implemented in Alfresco as a series of Web Scripts.<br></p>
         <p>Since 2006, Web Scripts proved themselves exceedingly useful and have been used in all kinds of solutions:<br></p>
         <br>
         <ul>
          <li> Integrating Alfresco with 3rd party systems<br></li>
          <li> Providing feeds<br></li>
          <li> Developing data services<br></li>
          <li> Allowing Alfresco to act as a different kind of repository (eg. ActiveResource)<br></li>
          <li> Developing UI services such as portlets<br></li>
          <li> Customizing search<br></li>
          <li> Acting as a back-end to client tools such as Orbean Forms<br></li>
          <li> Office integration<br></li>
          <li> Facebook application development<br></li>
          <li> UI component building in Alfresco SURF, a web site construction platform<br></li>
         </ul>
         <h1>What's new in Web Scripts v3?</h1>
         <br>
         <ul>
          <li> Web Script framework now a <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework%23Architecture" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">stand-alone component</a> allowing it to host Web Scripts in tiers other than the Alfresco Repository e.g. within <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FSurf_Platform" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Alfresco SURF</a><br></li>
          <li> <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23URI_Templates" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">URI Templates</a> now comply with JSR-311 (JAX-RS)<br></li>
          <li> <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Creating_a_Description_Document" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Run As</a> User<br></li>
          <li> Ability to Customize Web Scripts with Web Script-specific <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Configuration" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Configuration</a><br></li>
          <li> Per Web Script <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Message_Bundles" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Message Bundle</a><br></li>
          <li> Improved <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Multi-part_Form_Processing" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Form Processing</a> (Multi-part Form fields also mapped to args/argsM)<br></li>
          <li> Access to <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Creating_a_Controller_Script" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Request Headers</a><br></li>
          <li> <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Request_Processing" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Request Body</a> Processing<br></li>
          <li> <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Content_Negotiation_and_Response_Formats" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Content Negotiation</a><br></li>
          <li> <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Advanced_Description_Options" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Declarative</a> and <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Runtime_Cache_Controls" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">programmatic</a> Cache Control<br></li>
          <li> Web Script <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Advanced_Description_Options" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Families</a><br></li>
          <li> Specialized <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Creating_a_New_Kind_of_Web_Script" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Kinds of Web Script</a><br></li>
         </ul>
         <h1>What is a Web Script?</h1>
         <br>
         <p>A Web Script is simply a service bound to a URI which responds to HTTP methods such as GET, POST, PUT and DELETE.&nbsp; While using the same underlying code, there are broadly two kinds of Web Scripts.<br></p>
         <br>
         <h2>Data Web Scripts</h2>
         <br>
         <p>Data Web Scripts encapsulate access and modification of content/data held in the repository therefore are provided and exposed only by the Alfresco Repository server. They provide a repository interface for client applications to query, retrieve, update and perform processes typically using document formats such as XML &amp; JSON. Out-of-the-box, Alfresco provides a series of Data Web Scripts e.g. for tagging, activities, site management... <br></p>
         <br>
         <h2>Presentation Web Scripts</h2>
         <br>
         <p>Presentation Web Scripts allow you to build user interfaces such as a dashlet for Alfresco Explorer or Alfresco Share, a portlet for a JSR-168 portal, a UI component within Alfresco SURF, a Web Site or a custom Application. They typically render HTML (and perhaps include browser hosted JavaScript). Unlike Data Web Scripts, Presentation Web Scripts may be hosted in the Alfresco Repository server or in a separate presentation server. When hosted separately, the Presentation Web Scripts interact with Data Web Scripts. Out-of-the-box, Alfresco provides a series of Presentation Web Scripts e.g. Portlets, Office Integration, SURF Components...<br></p>
         <p>See the <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts_FAQ" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Web Scripts FAQ</a> for more information.<br></p>
         <br>
         <h2>Implementation</h2>
         <br>
         <p>The interface of a Web Script comprises of a URI, HTTP methods, and document types. This is all you need to know if you're just using a pre-built Web Script. However, if you want build your own RESTful interface, it has been made as simple as possible to construct your own Web Script. You do not need tooling or Java knowledge. All you need is your favourite text editor or Alfresco Explorer: no compilation, generators, server restarts, or complex installs.<br></p>
         <p>A Web Script implementation consists of the following components (often summarized as MVC):<br></p>
         <br>
         <ul>
          <li> A description document, which describes the URI that will initiate the script. For example, the service is given a short name and description, along with authentication and transactional needs. URI bindings are described as <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fbitworking.org%2Fnews%2FURI_Templates" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">URI templates</a>.<br></li>
         </ul>
         <ul>
          <li> An optional <strong><a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Creating_a_Controller_Script" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">controller script</a></strong>, written in JavaScript, which will do the actual work. For example, the script may query the Alfresco repository to build a set of data items, known as a <strong>model</strong> to render in the response, or for URIs that intend to modify the repository (hopefully, PUT, POST &amp; DELETE method bindings), the script may update the Alfresco repository. The JavaScript has access to all URI arguments, Alfresco services and repository data entry points.<br></li>
         </ul>
         <ul>
          <li> One or more FreeMarker <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Creating_a_Response_Template" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">response templates</a>, known as <strong>views</strong> (or Representations in REST parlance) that will render output in the correct format for your specific needs. For example, HTML, ATOM, XML, RSS, JSON, CSV, or any combination of these. The URL response is rendered via one of the supplied templates where the chosen template is based on the required response content-type or status outcome. The template has access to all URI arguments, common repository data entry points and any data items built by the optional controller script.<br></li>
         </ul>
         <p>Advanced implementations may fall-back to Java.&nbsp; The different components (description doc, controller, and templates) are tied together through a document convention. <br></p>
         <p>Web Scripts are registered and executed by the <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Web Scripts Framework</a>.<br></p>
         <br>
         <h1>Alfresco RESTful API Reference</h1>
         <br>
         <p>Out-of-the-box, Alfresco provides several RESTful APIs (built as Web Scripts):<br></p>
         <br>
         <ul>
          <li> <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FRepository_RESTful_API_Reference" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Repository API Reference</a> - remote services for interacting with the Alfresco Repository<br></li>
          <li> TODO: References to older and future versions of API?<br></li>
          <li> <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FOpenSearch" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">OpenSearch</a><br></li>
          <li> <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FCMIS_Web_Scripts_Reference" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">CMIS API Reference</a> - Content Management Interoperability Services<br></li>
          <li> <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F2.1_REST_API%23Package%3A%2Forg%2Falfresco%2Fportlets" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Portlets</a> such as My Inbox, My Checked-Out for hosting in any Portal<br></li>
          <li> <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F2.1_REST_API%23Package%3A%2Forg%2Falfresco%2Foffice" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Office Integration</a> for hosting in Microsoft Office<br></li>
         </ul>
         <h1>How Do I Use a Web Script?</h1>
         <br>
         <p>This section focuses on using pre-built Web Scripts. You will need to understand:<br></p>
         <br>
         <ul>
          <li> What is a URI<br></li>
          <li> How to invoke HTTP methods such GET &amp; POST from your environment of choice<br></li>
          <li> Optionally, how to construct or parse XML &amp; JSON if using Data Web Scripts<br></li>
         </ul>
         <p>Basically, Web scripts are URI &amp; HTTP accessible, so it is a case of putting together the correct HTTP request.&nbsp; Each Web Script is uniquely identified by its URI, although some Web Scripts may support multiple URIs.<br></p>
         <br>
         <h2>Where Can I Use a Web Script?</h2>
         <br>
         <p>Web Scripts may be used in a number of environments:<br></p>
         <br>
         <ul>
          <li> <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework%23Servlet_Runtime" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">HTTP Client</a> (e.g. Web Browser, HTTP Client API)<br></li>
          <li> <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FSurf_Platform" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Alfresco SURF</a><br></li>
          <li> Alfresco Explorer web client<br></li>
          <li> <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework%23JSR-168_Runtime" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">JSR-168 Portal</a><br></li>
          <li> <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework%23JSF_Runtime" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">JSF Page</a><br></li>
          <li> <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FFacebook" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Facebook Application</a><br></li>
         </ul>
         <h2>Anatomy of a Web Script URI</h2>
         <br>
         <p>Web Script URIs are of the form:<br></p>
         <pre>http[s]://&lt;host&gt;:&lt;port&gt;/[&lt;contextPath&gt;/]/&lt;servicePath&gt;<a class="" href="https://community.alfresco.com/<scriptPath>">/&lt;scriptPath&gt;</a>[?&lt;scriptArgs&gt;]<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>Where:<br></p>
         <pre>host - name or address of server hosting the Web Script<br>port - port where Web Script is exposed on server<br>contextPath - path where application is deployed to, generally /alfresco<br>servicePath - path where Web Script service is mapped to, generally /service<br>scriptPath - path to Web Script (as defined by Web Script)<br>scriptArgs - arguments to pass to Web Script<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>Some examples:<br></p>
         <pre>http://localhost:8080/alfresco/service/api/path/Workspace/SpacesStore/Company%20Home/children<br>http://localhost:8081/share/service/mytasks?priority=1<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>Depending on where a Web Script is invoked, the URI may be absolute or relative.&nbsp; In some cases Web Scripts may be deployed to the root application which means the <tt>contextPath</tt> is not required.<br></p>
         <pre>http://localhost:8080/service/api/path/Workspace/SpacesStore/Company%20Home/children<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>Some environments (such as <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FSurf_Platform" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Alfresco SURF</a> and the Web Script <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework%23JSR-168_Runtime" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Portal Runtime</a>) only require the script path to identify a Web Script.<br></p>
         <pre>/api/path/Workspace/SpacesStore/Company%20Home/children<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>The <tt>servicePath</tt> is generally mapped to <tt>/service</tt>. However, the means for <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts%23Authenticating" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">authenticating</a> may be controlled via this path.<br></p>
         <br>
         <h2>Listing Available Web Scripts</h2>
         <br>
         <p>An index of all registered Web Scripts is available at the following URIs:<br></p>
         <pre>http://&lt;host&gt;:&lt;port&gt;/&lt;contextPath&gt;/&lt;servicePath&gt;/<br>http://&lt;host&gt;:&lt;port&gt;/&lt;contextPath&gt;/&lt;servicePath&gt;/index<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>Example:<br></p>
         <pre>http://localhost:8080/alfresco/service/index<br>http://localhost:8081/share/service/index<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>A description of each registered Web Script is provided including its URI(s) for calling the Web Script. Some URIs contain {tokens} - those are also valid URIs - they are expressed as <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts%23URI_Templates" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">URI Templates</a> allowing for the URI path to be parameterized.<br></p>
         <p>The index provides a view of Web Scripts by:<br></p>
         <br>
         <ul>
          <li> Package<br></li>
          <li> URI<br></li>
          <li> Family<br></li>
         </ul>
         <p>Also, if there happens to be an issue with the registration of a Web Script, the index also provides a list of Web Scripts that failed registration.<br></p>
         <p><em>Note: This index page is itself implemented as a Web Script</em><br><br><em>Note: The <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%232.1_REST_API" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Alfresco RESTful API Reference</a> pages in this WIKI are just index pages rendered as MediaWIKI markup instead of HTML</em><br></p>
         <br>
         <h2>Authenticating</h2>
         <br>
         <p>Web Scripts may require the caller to be authenticated. Each Web Script dictates its own authentication requirements. If a Web Script requires authenticated access and the call is unauthenticated an appropriate authentication process is initiated. Upon successful authentication the Web Script is invoked.<br></p>
         <p>The style of authentication depends on the environment within which the Web Script is hosted e.g. within a servlet run-time HTTP Auth may be used. Within a portal run-time, the portal may decide.&nbsp; <br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            Repository Authentication Options
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <p>When Web Scripts are hosted within the Repository server two options are available for authentication.<br></p>
         <br>
         <ol>
          <li> HTTP BASIC Authentication - the authentication process follows the handshake as defined by <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Ftools.ietf.org%2Fhtml%2Frfc2617" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">RFC2617</a><br></li>
          <li> Alfresco Explorer Authentication - the authentication process supported by the Explorer Web Client, that is the authentication mechanism as defined by the alfresco global properties <em>authentication.chain</em>.<br></li>
         </ol>
         <p>The first is useful for external systems that wish to programmatically invoke Alfresco RESTfully (that is, using standard HTTP mechanisms), whereas the second is useful when single sign on is required across both the Alfresco Explorer Client and the Web Script, such as linking from the Explorer to a Web Script page. <br></p>
         <p>The caller can choose which authentication option by specifying an appropriate &lt;servicePath&gt; in the Web Script URI.<br></p>
         <br>
         <ol>
          <li> /service =&gt; HTTP Basic Authentication e.g. <tt><a class="jive-link-external-small" href="http://localhost:8080/" rel="nofollow">http://localhost:8080/</a><strong>service</strong>/api/path/Workspace/SpacesStore/Company%20Home/children</tt><br></li>
          <li> /wcservice =&gt; Alfresco Explorer Authentication e.g. <tt><a class="jive-link-external-small" href="http://localhost:8080/" rel="nofollow">http://localhost:8080/</a><strong>wcservice</strong>/api/path/Workspace/SpacesStore/Company%20Home/children</tt><br></li>
         </ol>
         <p><em>Note: In both cases, the successful authentication may be remembered in the caller session, thus only requiring the authentication process to be initiated once</em><br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            Pre-Authorized Calls
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <p>To force authenticated access specify the following URI argument:<br></p>
         <pre>alf_ticket=&lt;ticket&gt;<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>For example<br></p>
         <pre>http://&lt;host&gt;:&lt;port&gt;/&lt;contextPath&gt;/&lt;servicePath&gt;/api/path/Workspace/SpacesStore/Company%20Home/children<strong>?alf_ticket=&lt;ticket&gt;</strong><br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>Tickets may be established by the calling environment (e.g. Alfresco SURF) or explicitly using the <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F2.1_REST_API%23Login" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Login Web Script APIs</a>.<br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            Guest Access
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <p>Web scripts may allow guest access.&nbsp; To force guest access specify the following URL argument:<br></p>
         <pre>guest=true<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>For example<br></p>
         <pre>http://&lt;host&gt;:&lt;port&gt;/&lt;contextPath&gt;/&lt;servicePath&gt;/api/path/Workspace/SpacesStore/Company%20Home<strong>?guest=true</strong><br></pre>
         <br>
         <h2>Content Negotiation and Response Formats</h2>
         <br>
         <p>Each Web Script returns its result in a reponse stream. The result may be encoded in one or more formats (i.e. mimetypes) such as HTML, XML or JSON depending on the capabilities of the invoked Web Script.<br></p>
         <p>If a Web Script call does not provide any hints on which response encoding to use, the Web Script uses its pre-defined default encoding. However, a client can provide the following hints:<br></p>
         <br>
         <ol>
          <li> URL extension e.g. <tt><a class="jive-link-external-small" href="http://" rel="nofollow">http://</a><span>&lt;host&gt;:&lt;port&gt;/&lt;contextPath&gt;/&lt;servicePath&gt;/api/path/Workspace/SpacesStore/Company%20Home/children</span><strong>.atom</strong></tt><br></li>
          <li> Format Argument e.g. <tt><a class="jive-link-external-small" href="http://" rel="nofollow">http://</a><span>&lt;host&gt;:&lt;port&gt;/&lt;contextPath&gt;/&lt;servicePath&gt;/api/path/Workspace/SpacesStore/Company%20Home/children</span><strong>?format=atom</strong></tt><br></li>
          <li> Accept Header (as defined by <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.w3.org%2FProtocols%2Frfc2616%2Frfc2616-sec14.html" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">HTTP 1.1</a>)<br></li>
         </ol>
         <p>Hints 1 &amp; 2 specify a Web Script Format which a <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework%23HTTP_Response_Formats" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">registered short name</a> for a mimetype. The typical mimetypes are mapped:<br></p>
         <br>
         <ul>
          <li> <strong>html</strong>&nbsp; =&gt; text/html<br></li>
          <li> <strong>text</strong> =&gt; text/plain<br></li>
          <li> <strong>xml</strong>&nbsp; =&gt; text/xml<br></li>
          <li> <strong>atom</strong>&nbsp; =&gt; application/atom+xml<br></li>
          <li> <strong>rss</strong>&nbsp; =&gt; application/rss+xml <br></li>
          <li> <strong>json</strong>&nbsp; =&gt; application/json<br></li>
         </ul>
         <p>Hint 3 is typically provided by a Web Browser, although may be controlled programmatically via many HTTP client libraries and is specified as a comma-separated of mimetypes and preferences.<br></p>
         <p><em>Note: Each Web Script dictates which of the above hints are adhered to via its Web Script Description</em><br></p>
         <br>
         <h2>Tunneling HTTP Methods</h2>
         <br>
         <p>Not all clients can issue all HTTP methods. In the most severe case, a client may be restricted to GET and POST only. In this situation, web scripts provide two mechanisms for issuing any HTTP method via POST:<br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            HTTP Request Header '
           <tt>X-HTTP-Method-Override</tt>'
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            URI parameter '
           <tt>alf_method</tt>'
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <p><i>Note: If both the header and query parameter are specified in the request, the <strong>header</strong> takes precedence over the query parameter.</i><br></p>
         <p>In either case, the value is set to the HTTP method name to be invoked.<br></p>
         <p>For example, if the HTTP DELETE method is not supported by a client, but the client wishes to delete a repository folder, the following may be issued:<br></p>
         <pre>POST X-HTTP-Method-Override=DELETE <tt>http://&lt;host&gt;:&lt;port&gt;/&lt;contextPath&gt;/&lt;servicePath&gt;/api/path/Workspace/SpacesStore/Company%20Home/</tt><br></pre>
         <br>
         <pre>POST <tt>http://&lt;host&gt;:&lt;port&gt;/&lt;contextPath&gt;/&lt;servicePath&gt;/api/path/Workspace/SpacesStore/Company%20Home?alf_method=DELETE</tt><br></pre>
         <br>
         <h2>Forcing Success Response Status</h2>
         <br>
         <p>Not all clients can gracefully handle non-success HTTP Responses, for example, the Flash runtime player - the runtime for Adobe Flex applications.<br></p>
         <p>In this situation, web scripts provide a mechanism to force all HTTP Responses to indicate success in their Response Header.&nbsp; However, the Response body will still represent the content as if a non-success status had occurred.<br></p>
         <p>To force HTTP Response Header success set the following HTTP Request Header:<br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt> 
           <tt>alf-force-success-response</tt> = 
           <tt>true</tt>
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <h2>JSON Callbacks</h2>
         <br>
         <p>If your web scripts provide JSON responses, it is likely they will be invoked directly from within a Web Browser via the XMLHttpRequest object. However, due to security reasons, you may run into cross-domain issues, a restriction that requires you to proxy your requests on the server side. Typically, to workaround these issues, public services such as <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fdeveloper.yahoo.com%2Fjavascript%2Fjson.html" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Yahoo! JSON Services</a> provide a callback mechanism.<br></p>
         <p>Web scripts also provide this mechanism which wraps the JSON output text in parentheses and a function name of your choosing. A callback is invoked by adding the following URL parameter on JSON URL requests:<br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            alf_callback=
           <i>function</i>
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <p>where <i>function</i> is the name of a client-side JavaScript function to be invoked.<br></p>
         <p>The following simple HTML page demonstrates this:<br></p>
         <pre><br>&nbsp;&nbsp; <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </pre>
         <br>
         <p>This will result in the JSON response looking like this:<br></p>
         <pre>showTitle( <i>...json output...</i> );<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p><strong>NOTE:</strong> For security reasons, this mechanism is disabled by default. To enable it on any SpringWebScripts container, set the bean property: allowCallbacks = true, for example:<br></p>
         <pre>&nbsp; &lt;bean id='webscripts.container' parent='webscripts.abstractcontainer' class='org.springframework.extensions.webscripts.PresentationContainer'&gt;<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &lt;property name='name'&gt;&lt;value&gt;Spring Web Scripts Container&lt;/value&gt;&lt;/property&gt;<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &lt;property name='allowCallbacks'&gt;&lt;value&gt;true&lt;/value&gt;&lt;/property&gt;<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; ...<br>&nbsp; &lt;/bean&gt;<br></pre>
         <br>
         <h2>Caching</h2>
         <br>
         <p>Web Scripts comply with <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.w3.org%2FProtocols%2Frfc2616%2Frfc2616-sec13.html" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">HTTP Caching</a> supporting the notions of Last Modified Time and ETag allowing a Web Script response to be cached. A cache manager (suitable for the client environment) can interpret the cache controls (if any) returned with the Web Script response and cache appropriately.<br></p>
         <p>A typical scenario is where a Repository-hosted Web Script is invoked via HTTP. In this case, any HTTP caching proxy may be used between the client and Alfresco Repository Server.<br></p>
         <p><em>Note: Each Web Script dictates its caching controls, if any</em><br></p>
         <br>
         <h1>How Do I Create a Web Script?</h1>
         <br>
         <p>This section demonstrates how to create a Web Script. The Web Script in question is a simple Hello World example requiring authenticated access which simply greets the user in both HTML and XML.<br></p>
         <p>You will need to understand:<br></p>
         <br>
         <ul>
          <li> XML for expressing the Web Script description<br></li>
          <li> Optionally, JavaScript for writing Web Script behaviour<br></li>
          <li> Freemarker for rendering a Web Script response<br></li>
         </ul>
         <p>The only tools you'll need are an Alfresco Repository server and the Alfresco Explorer web client. Alternatively, advanced Web Scripts may be <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Java-Backed_Implementations" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">developed in Java</a>.<br></p>
         <br>
         <h2>Examples and Guidelines</h2>
         <br>
         <p>Before diving into the technical bit, you may want to browse or refer to the available <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts_Examples" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Web Scripts Examples</a>.<br></p>
         <p>If you're really impatient, you can create your <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts_Hello_World_Quick_Start" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">first Web Script</a> within the next minute or so.<br></p>
         <p>You may also wish to refer to the Alfresco guidelines for <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FAlfresco_REST_Design_Guidelines" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">designing RESTful Web Scripts</a>.<br></p>
         <br>
         <h2>Choosing a URI</h2>
         <br>
         <p>First, choose a URI and HTTP method for your Hello World Web Script...<br></p>
         <pre>GET /&lt;contextPath&gt;/&lt;servicePath&gt;/sample/helloworld?to={name?}<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>The URI is under your control, but must be unique. <br></p>
         <p><strong>Note</strong> the following URL namespaces are reserved for Alfresco use:<br></p>
         <pre>/&lt;contextPath&gt;/&lt;servicePath&gt;/sample<br>/&lt;contextPath&gt;/&lt;servicePath&gt;/api<br>/&lt;contextPath&gt;/&lt;servicePath&gt;/ui<br>/&lt;contextPath&gt;/&lt;servicePath&gt;/office<br>/&lt;contextPath&gt;/&lt;servicePath&gt;/wcm<br></pre>
         <br>
         <h2>Deciding Where to Place Web Script Implementation</h2>
         <br>
         <p>With a URI decided, it is necessary to bind a Web Script implementation to it, consisting of the following files:<br></p>
         <br>
         <ol>
          <li> A Description Document<br></li>
          <li> A Controller Script (optional)<br></li>
          <li> One or more Response Templates<br></li>
          <li> A Configuration Document (optional)<br></li>
          <li> A Locale Bundle (optional)<br></li>
         </ol>
         <p>Our example Hello World implementation will consist of the following files:<br></p>
         <pre><a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Creating_a_Description_Document" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">helloworld.get.desc.xml</a><br><a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Creating_a_Controller_Script" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">helloworld.get.js</a><br><a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Creating_a_Response_Template" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">helloworld.get.html.ftl</a><br><a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Multiple_Response_Formats" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">helloworld.get.xml.ftl</a><br><a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Response_Status" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">helloworld.get.html.400.ftl</a><br><a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Response_Status" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">helloworld.get.xml.400.ftl</a><br><a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Web_Script_Configuration" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">helloworld.get.config.xml</a><br><a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Message_Bundles" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">helloworld.get.properties</a><br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>These files need to be stored in a folder somewhere. They can live in either the Alfresco Repository or the Java ClassPath.&nbsp; The following folders are listed in the sequence in which Alfresco searches for Web Script implementation files:<br></p>
         <br>
         <ol>
          <li> repository folder: <code>/Company Home/Data Dictionary/Web Scripts Extensions</code><br></li>
          <li> repository folder: <code>/Company Home/Data Dictionary/Web Scripts</code><br></li>
          <li> class path folder: <code>/alfresco/extension/templates/webscripts</code><br></li>
          <li> class path folder: <code>/alfresco/templates/webscripts</code><br></li>
         </ol>
         <p>Within any of these folders, you can use subfolders to organize web scripts.<br></p>
         <p>New web scripts will not be visible until the 'Refresh Web Scripts' link is clicked on the /alfresco/service/ page.<br></p>
         <p><strong>Warning!</strong> do not store web scripts in:<br></p>
         <pre>/org/alfresco<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>or any of its subfolders - these folders are reserved for Alfresco use.<br></p>
         <br>
         <h2>Creating a Description Document</h2>
         <br>
         <p>Our URI is described by creating an .xml description document in one of the above Web Script folders. For now, assume all files are placed into the repository folder: <tt>/Company Home/Data Dictionary/Web Scripts</tt>.<br></p>
         <p>Within any Web Script folder, sub-folders may be used to organise Web Scripts. For example, we can place our Hello World Web Script in the folder<br></p>
         <pre>/Company Home/Data Dictionary/Web Scripts/org/alfresco/sample<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>and within this folder, create the file<br></p>
         <pre>helloworld.get.desc.xml<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>Naming is important. Web Scripts employ convention over configuration for their definition to reduce the amount of required typing. The postfix <tt>.desc.xml</tt> informs Alfresco that this is a Web Script description document.<br></p>
         <p>The complete folder and file name<br></p>
         <pre><strong>org/alfresco/sample/helloworld</strong>.<strong>get</strong>.desc.xml<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>defines<br></p>
         <br>
         <ol>
          <li> A package of <strong>org/alfresco/sample</strong><br></li>
          <li> A service id of <strong>helloworld</strong><br></li>
          <li> A binding to the HTTP <strong>GET</strong> method<br></li>
         </ol>
         <p><br><br>The content of the Hello World Web Script description document is defined as follows:<br></p>
         <pre>&lt;webscript&gt;<br>&nbsp; &lt;shortname&gt;Hello World&lt;/shortname&gt;<br>&nbsp; &lt;description&gt;Greet a user&lt;/description&gt;<br>&nbsp; &lt;url&gt;/helloworld?to={name?}&lt;/url&gt;<br>&nbsp; &lt;url&gt;/hello/world?to={name?}&lt;/url&gt;<br>&nbsp; &lt;format default='html'&gt;extension&lt;/format&gt;<br>&nbsp; &lt;authentication&gt;user&lt;/authentication&gt;<br>&lt;/webscript&gt;<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>Where:<br></p>
         <br>
         <ul>
          <li> <tt>shortname</tt> is a human readable name for the Web Script<br></li>
          <li> <tt>description</tt> (optional) is documentation for the Web Script<br></li>
          <li> <tt>url</tt> (one or more) is a <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts%23URI_Templates" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">URI Template</a> to which the Web Script is bound; variants of the URI template which specify a format do not need to be registered, however, they are useful for documentation purposes<br></li>
          <li> <tt>format</tt> (optional) controls how the content-type of the response can be specified via the URI; valid values are:<br>
           <ul>
            <li> <tt>argument</tt> the content-type is specified via the <tt>format</tt> query string parameter, for example <tt>/helloworld?to=dave&amp;<strong>format=xml</strong></tt><br></li>
            <li> <tt>extension</tt> the content-type is specified via the URI extension, for example <tt>/hello/world<strong>.xml</strong>?to=dave</tt><br></li>
            <li> <tt>any</tt> either of the above can be used<br></li>
            <li> Note: if not specified, the default value is <tt>any</tt><br></li>
            <li> Note: if the caller does not specify a required content-type at all, the default content-type is taken from the (optional) <tt>default</tt> attribute of the <tt>format</tt> element. By default, if not set, the html format is assumed. In some cases, a URI may decide upon a response content-type at runtime. For these URIs, specify an empty format, for example <tt>format default=''</tt><br></li>
           </ul></li>
          <li> <tt>authentication</tt> (optional) is the required level of authentication; valid values are:<br>
           <ul>
            <li> <tt>none</tt> specifies that no authentication is required at all<br></li>
            <li> <tt>guest</tt> specifies that at least guest authentication is required<br></li>
            <li> <tt>user</tt> specifies that at least named user authentication is required<br></li>
