            <li> <tt>admin</tt> specifies that at least a named admin authentication is required<br></li>
            <li> Note: if not specified, the default value is <tt>none</tt><br></li>
            <li> Note: The optional runas attribute can be used to force the execution of a web script as a specific user. This can only be specified for web scripts that are stored in the Java Class path.<br></li>
           </ul></li>
         </ul>
         <p>The description provides Alfresco with all the necessary information to bind the web script to one or more URIs.&nbsp; It also provides enough to document the Web Script.<br></p>
         <br>
         <h2>Advanced Description Options</h2>
         <br>
         <p>Description documents also provide the following options, which are important, but not as frequently used or mandated.<br></p>
         <br>
         <ul>
          <li> <tt>transaction</tt> (optional) is the required level transaction; valid values are:<br>
           <ul>
            <li> <tt>none</tt> specifies that no transaction is required at all<br></li>
            <li> <tt>required</tt> specifies that a transaction is required (and will inherit an existing transaction, if open)<br></li>
            <li> <tt>requiresnew</tt> specifies that a new transaction is required<br></li>
            <li> Note: If not specified, the default value is <tt>none</tt> if <tt>authentication</tt> is also <tt>none</tt>, otherwise the value is <tt>required</tt><br></li>
           </ul></li>
          <li> <tt>family</tt> (optional) is a tag for categorizing similar or related web scripts. The family tag may be repeated if this script belongs to more than one family.<br></li>
          <li> <tt>cache</tt> (optional) is the required level of caching; valid child elements are:<br>
           <ul>
            <li> <tt>never</tt> (optional) specifies whether caching should be applied at all; valid values (optional) are:<br>
             <ul>
              <li> <tt>true</tt> (default) specifies the web script response should never be cached<br></li>
              <li> <tt>false</tt> specifies the web script response may be cached<br></li>
              <li> Note: If <tt>never</tt> is not specified, the default is <tt>true</tt><br></li>
             </ul></li>
            <li> <tt>public</tt> (optional) specifies whether authenticated responses should be cached in a public cache; valid values (optional) are:<br>
             <ul>
              <li> <tt>true</tt> (default) specifies the web script authenticated response may be cached in a public cache<br></li>
              <li> <tt>false</tt> specifies the web script authenticated response may not be cached in a public cache<br></li>
              <li> Note: If <tt>public</tt> is not specified, the default is <tt>false</tt><br></li>
             </ul></li>
            <li> <tt>mustrevalidate</tt> (optional) specifies whether a cache must revalidate its version of the web script response in order to ensure freshness; valid values (optional) are:<br>
             <ul>
              <li> <tt>true</tt> (default) specifies that validation must occur<br></li>
              <li> <tt>false</tt> specifies that validation may occur<br></li>
              <li> Note: If <tt>mustrevalidate</tt> is not specified, the default is <tt>true</tt><br></li>
             </ul></li>
           </ul></li>
          <li> <tt>negotiate</tt> (zero or more) associates an Accept header MIME type to a specific web script format of response; the (mandatory) value specifies the format while the mandatory <tt>accept</tt> attribute specifies the MIME type<br>
           <ul>
            <li> Note: Content Negotiation is enabled with the definition of at least one <tt>negotiate</tt> element<br></li>
           </ul></li>
          <li> <tt>kind</tt> (optional) is an attribute discriminator for overriding the <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Creating_a_New_Kind_of_Web_Script" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">kind of web script</a>. See list of <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Kinds" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">available web script kinds</a>.<br></li>
         </ul>
         <ul>
          <li> <tt>lifecycle</tt> (optional) is an attribute for describing the <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Script_Lifecycle_" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">lifecycle</a> of the web script. Web scripts typically start out in some sort of draft state, are promoted to full production use, and are then retired at the end of their life.<br>
           <ul>
            <li> <tt>none</tt>This web script is not part of a lifecycle.<br></li>
            <li> <tt>sample</tt> This web script is a sample and is not intended for production use.<br></li>
            <li> <tt>draft</tt> This method may be incomplete, experimental, or still subject to change.<br></li>
            <li> <tt>public_api</tt> This method is part of the Alfresco public API and should be stable and well tested.<br></li>
            <li> <tt>draft_public_api</tt> This method is intended to eventually become part of the public API but is incomplete or still subject to change.<br></li>
            <li> <tt>deprecated</tt> This method should be avoided. It may be removed in future versions of Alfresco.<br></li>
            <li> <tt>internal</tt> This script is for Alfresco use only. This script should not be relied upon between versions. It is likely to change.<br></li>
           </ul></li>
         </ul>
         <p>An example of a full web script description follows:<br></p>
         <pre>&lt;webscript <strong>kind='org.alfresco.httpsonly'</strong>&gt; <br>&nbsp; &lt;shortname&gt;Hello World&lt;/shortname&gt;<br>&nbsp; &lt;description&gt;Greet a user&lt;/description&gt;<br>&nbsp; &lt;url&gt;/sample/helloworld?to={name}&lt;/url&gt;<br>&nbsp; &lt;url&gt;/sample/helloworld.xml?to={name}&lt;/url&gt;<br>&nbsp; &lt;format default='html'&gt;extension&lt;/format&gt;<br>&nbsp; &lt;lifecycle&gt;sample&lt;/lifecycle&gt;<br>&nbsp; &lt;authentication <strong>runas='fred'</strong>&gt;user&lt;/authentication&gt;<br>&nbsp; <strong>&lt;transaction&gt;required&lt;/transaction&gt;</strong><br>&nbsp; <strong>&lt;family&gt;Sample&lt;/family&gt;</strong><br>&nbsp; <strong>&lt;cache&gt;</strong><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <strong>&lt;never&gt;false&lt;/never&gt;</strong><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <strong>&lt;public&gt;false&lt;/public&gt;</strong><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <strong>&lt;mustrevalidate/&gt;</strong><br>&nbsp; <strong>&lt;/cache&gt;</strong><br>&nbsp; <strong>&lt;negotiate accept='text/html'&gt;html&lt;/negotiate&gt;</strong><br>&nbsp; <strong>&lt;negotiate accept='text/xml'&gt;xml&lt;/negotiate&gt;</strong><br>&lt;/webscript&gt;<br></pre>
         <br>
         <h2>URI Templates</h2>
         <br>
         <p>A URI template is simply a URI containing tokens which may be substituted with actual values. The URI template <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fjcp.org%2Fen%2Fjsr%2Fdetail%3Fid%3D311" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">syntax</a> is minimal and simple, and as of Alfresco v3, complies with the template syntax of JSR-311 (JAX-RS). Common forms of URI template include:<br></p>
         <p><code><br></code></p>
         <pre>/content/a/b/c/d.txt<br>/sample/helloworld?to={name?}<br>/blog/search?q={searchTerm}&amp;amp;n={numResults}<br>/people/{personName}/profile/{profileStyle}<br>/blog/category/{category}?n={itemsperpage?}<br>/user/{userid}<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p><br></p>
         <p>A token of the form {&lt;name&gt;?} means it is optional. Typically, tokens are used for URI arguments, but may also be used for path segments.<br></p>
         <p>Note the third example passes two parameters to the Web Script. Normally an ampersand (&amp;) is used to separate parameters, though in your XML Web Script Description document one must use the escaped literal '&amp;amp;' instead.<br></p>
         <p>For now, Web Scripts do not enforce mandatory arguments. However, it is still useful to provide a full URI template for documentation purposes.<br></p>
         <p>URI templates are specified relative to <tt><a class="jive-link-external-small" href="http://" rel="nofollow">http://</a><span>&lt;host&gt;:&lt;port&gt;/&lt;contextPath&gt;/&lt;servicePath&gt;</span></tt>.<br></p>
         <p>When a URI request is made, Alfresco locates the appropriate Web Script by finding the closest match to a URI template in a Web Script description document. <br></p>
         <p>Given the following URI Templates:<br></p>
         <pre>1 <tt>/a</tt><br>2 <tt>/a/b</tt><br>3 <tt>/a/{val1}</tt><br>4 <tt>/a/{val1}/b</tt><br>5 <tt>/a/{val1}/b/{val1}</tt><br>6 <tt>/a/{val1}/b/{val2}</tt><br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>The following URIs match the above templates as follows:<br></p>
         <pre>/a =&gt; template 1<br>/a/b =&gt; template 2<br>/a/c =&gt; template 3<br>/a/b/b =&gt; template 4<br>/a/c/b =&gt; template 4<br>/a/c/b/c =&gt; template 5<br>/a/c/b/d =&gt; template 6<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>However, the following URIs do not match any of the above templates:<br></p>
         <pre>/b<br>/a/c/c<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>As an implementor of a Web Script you have access to the values provided for tokens in the URI template e.g. access to the values for <tt>{val1}</tt> and <tt>{val2}</tt>. The values are available in both the Web Script <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Creating_a_Controller_Script" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Controller Script</a> and <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Creating_a_Response_Template" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Response Templates</a> via the root object <tt><a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23url" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">url.templateArgs</a></tt>.<br><br>When using java backed controllers the tokens can be accessed through the <code>org.alfresco.web.scripts.WebScriptRequest.getServiceMatch()</code> API. In Community Edition 3.2r2 this will return a <code>org.alfresco.web.scripts.Match</code> instance that has a <code>getTemplateVars()</code> method returning a Map of all tokens.<br></p>
         <br>
         <h2>Creating a Controller Script</h2>
         <br>
         <p>A Web Script may optionally execute some JavaScript on invocation of its respective URI. The JavaScript can perform queries or updates against a back-end store. Also, the JavaScript may build a data model that is passed to the appropriate Web Script response template for subsequent response rendering.<br></p>
         <p>For our example Hello World service we create the following file in the same folder as the Web Script description document<br></p>
         <pre>helloworld.get.js<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>Again, naming conventions apply where controller script file names have the following structure<br></p>
         <pre>&lt;serviceId&gt;.&lt;httpMethod&gt;.js<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>The following JavaScript root objects are available to all Web Scripts, regardless of their hosting environment.<br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            args: an associative array of all URI parameters. See 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts_Examples%23URL_Argument_Handling" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">example</a>.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            argsM: an associative array of all URI parameters (where each key is an argument name and each value is an array containing all respective argument values, even if only one is supplied). See 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts_Examples%23URL_Argument_Handling" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">example</a>.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            headers: an associative array of all request headers.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            headersM: an associative array of all request headers (where each key is an header name and each value is an array containing all respective header values, even if only one is supplied). See 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts_Examples%23URL_Argument_Handling" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">example</a>.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt> 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23url" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">url</a>: provides access to the URI (or parts of the URI) that triggered the web script.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            model: An empty associative array which may be populated by the JavaScript. Values placed into this array are available as root objects in Web Script response templates.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt> 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23status" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">status</a>: provides ability to control response status codes.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt> 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23cache" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">cache</a>: provides ability to control caching of response.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt> 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Web_Script_Configuration" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">config</a>: provides access to the Web Script configuration.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            msg: provides access to Web Script localized messages.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt> 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23format" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">format</a>: provides information on the response format to be rendered.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            guest: A boolean indicating whether the web script is executing as 'Guest'.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt> 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23webscript" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">webscript</a>: An associative array of meta-data properties describing the Web Script.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt> 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23server" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">server</a>: An associative array of meta-data properties describing the server hosting the Web Script.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt> 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23json" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">jsonUtils</a>: A host object for parsing and generating JSON objects.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt> 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23atom" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">atom</a>: A host object for parsing and generating Atom (Publishing) documents.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            logger: A host object providing access to console logging facilities for debugging of scripts. See the 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FJavaScript_API%23Logging_API" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Logging API</a>. 
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <p>Web Scripts hosted within the Alfresco Repository tier also have access to the following root objects which provide direct access to Repository services and content.<br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            roothome: the repository root node (only available if authenticated)
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            companyhome: the company home folder (only available if authenticated)
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            person: the person node of the currently authenticated user (only available if authenticated)
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            userhome: the user home folder (only available if authenticated)
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            search: A host object providing access to Lucene and Saved Search results. See the 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FJavaScript_API%23Search_API" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Search API</a>.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            people: A host object providing access to Alfresco people and groups. See the 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FJavaScript_API%23People_API" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">People API</a>.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            actions: A host object providing invocation of registered Alfresco Actions. See the 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FJavaScript_API%23Actions_API" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Actions API</a>.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            session: Session related information such as the current authentication ticket. See the 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FJavaScript_API%23Session_API" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Session API</a>.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            classification: Access to the root elements of the classification API. See the 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FJavaScript_API%23Classification_API" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Classification API</a>.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            utils: Access to a library of useful helper functions not provided as part of generic JavaScript. See the 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FJavaScript_API%23Utility_Functions" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Utility Functions</a>.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            avm: Access to WCM objects such as AVM paths and searching within AVM stores and web projects. See the 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FJavaScript_API%23AVM_API" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">AVM API</a>.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            crossRepoCopy: Cross repository copy support. See the 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FJavaScript_API%23Cross_Repository_Copy" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Cross Repository Copy</a>.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            workflow: Start workflows and access, control in-flight workflows.&nbsp; See the 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FJavaScript_API%23Workflow_API" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">JavaScript API#Workflow API</a>.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <p>Web Scripts hosted within the presentation tier (i.e. within Alfresco SURF) have their own extras as described in the <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FSurf_Platform_-_Freemarker_Template_and_JavaScript_API" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Surf Platform - Freemarker Template and JavaScript API</a>. <br></p>
         <p>For our example Hellow World, we can write the following JavaScript to either greet the currently authenticated user via their user name, or via the name provided as an URI argument:<br></p>
         <pre>model.toWho = (args.to&nbsp;!= null)&nbsp;? args.to&nbsp;: person.properties.userName; <br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>The result of the script is added to the <tt>model</tt> root object and given the name <tt>who</tt>. Web Script response templates rendered after the execution of the JavaScript will now also have the root object named <tt>who</tt>, which in this case represents the name of the person to greet.<br></p>
         <p>Of course, a Web Script can also perform updates, in which case, the <tt>model</tt> root object can be used to record items that have been updated, status, and so on.<br></p>
         <br>
         <h2>Debugging a Controller Script</h2>
         <br>
         <p>The Alfresco Server provides a built-in <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FJavaScript_API%23Alfresco_Javascript_Debugger" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Javascript debugger</a>.<br></p>
         <br>
         <h2>Creating a Response Template</h2>
         <br>
         <p>The final stage of a Web Script is to render a response for the HTTP request. Multiple response formats may be provided. Responses are rendered by FreeMarker templates.<br></p>
         <p>For our example Hello World service, we create the following file in the same folder as the Web Script description document<br></p>
         <pre>helloworld.get.html.ftl<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>Again, naming conventions apply where response template file names have the following structure<br></p>
         <pre>&lt;serviceId&gt;.&lt;httpMethod&gt;.&lt;format&gt;.ftl<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>where<br></p>
         <br>
         <ul>
          <li> <tt>format</tt> specifies the format of the response template whose value is one of the following <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts_Framework%23HTTP_Response_Formats" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">formats</a>.<br></li>
         </ul>
         <p>The following FreeMarker template root objects are available to all Web Scripts, regardless of their hosting environment. <br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            args: an associative array of all URI parameters. See 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts_Examples%23URL_Argument_Handling" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">example</a>.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            argsM: an associative array of all URI parameters (where each key is an argument name and each value is an array containing all argument values, even if only one is supplied). See 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts_Examples%23URL_Argument_Handling" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">example</a>.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            headers: an associative array of all request headers.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            headersM: an associative array of all request headers (where each key is an header name and each value is an array containing all respective header values, even if only one is supplied). See 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts_Examples%23URL_Argument_Handling" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">example</a>.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt> 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23url" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">url</a>: provides access to the URI (or parts of the URI) that triggered the web script.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt> 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23status" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">status</a>: provides ability to control response status codes.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt> 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23cache" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">cache</a>: provides ability to control caching of response.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt> 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Web_Script_Configuration" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">config</a>: provides access to Web Script configuration.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            messages: a JSON representation of all localized messages for the Web Script.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt> 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23format" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">format</a>: provides information on the response format to be rendered.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            guest: A boolean indicating whether the web script is executing as 'Guest'.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt> 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23webscript" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">webscript</a>: An associative array of meta-data properties describing the Web Script.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt> 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23server" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">server</a>: An associative array of meta-data properties describing the server hosting the Web Script.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            date: A date representing the date and time of the web script request.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <p>Web Scripts hosted within the Alfresco Repository tier also have access to the following template root objects which provide direct access to Repository services and content.<br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            roothome: the repository root node (only available if authenticated)
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            companyhome: the company home folder (only available if authenticated)
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            person: the person node of the currently authenticated user (only available if authenticated)
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            userhome: the user home folder (only available if authenticated)
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <p>Web Scripts hosted within the presentation tier (i.e. within Alfresco SURF) have their own extras as described in the <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FSurf_Platform_-_Freemarker_Template_and_JavaScript_API" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Surf Platform - Freemarker Template and JavaScript API</a>. <br></p>
         <p>And remember, the FreeMarker template also has access to any root objects created by the controller script, if one has been associated with the Web Script.<br></p>
         <p>Web script templates also have access to the following methods:<br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            absurl(url): Returns an absolute URL representation of the passed url. Useful when rendering links within ATOM (and similar formats).
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            xmldate(date): Returns an ISO8601 formatted result of the passed date. Useful when rendering dates within XML.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            scripturl(queryString): Returns a url that references this web script. The passed 
           <tt>queryString</tt> is added to the url. System arguments such as 
           <tt>guest</tt> and 
           <tt>format</tt> are automatically added. Note, this method is particularly useful for protection against the runtime environment within which the web script is executing. In some environments (such as a Portal) the url may be encoded.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            clienturlfunction(funcName): Generates a client-side JavaScript function that can generate a URL back to this web script.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            argreplace(argString, argName, argValue, ...): Replace specified argName with argValue, or add argName if it does not exist in argString.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            encodeuri(uriString): encode string into URL-safe form.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <p>For our example blog search, we can write the following FreeMarker to render the HTML response:<br></p>
         <pre><br>&nbsp;&nbsp; <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; At ${date?datetime}, ${person.properties.userName} says hello to ${toWho?html}<br>&nbsp;&nbsp; <br> <br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>Note how the above template makes use of standard root objects, for example <strong>${date?datetime}</strong> and root objects created by the controller script, for example <strong>${toWho?html}</strong>.<br></p>
         <br>
         <h2>Multiple Response Formats</h2>
         <br>
         <p>Multiple response formats are simply supported by creating further template files following the naming convention outlined above.<br></p>
         <p><em>Note: New and updated Templates are automatically registered and will be honoured when the Web Script is next invoked.</em><br></p>
         <p>For our Hello World example, we can support add a machine-readable XML response by adding the following file<br></p>
         <pre>helloworld.get.xml.ftl<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>whose content is<br></p>
         <pre>&lt;helloworld&gt;<br>&nbsp; &lt;from&gt;${person.properties.userName}&lt;/from&gt;<br>&nbsp; &lt;says&gt;hello&lt;/says&gt;<br>&nbsp; &lt;to&gt;${toWho?xml}&lt;/to&gt;<br>&lt;/helloworld&gt;<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>With our Hello World example description document and associated templates, the following URI mappings are available:<br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            HTML template: 
           <tt>/&lt;contextPath&gt;/&lt;servicePath&gt;/sample/helloworld?to=friend</tt>
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            HTML template: 
           <tt>/&lt;contextPath&gt;/&lt;servicePath&gt;/sample/helloworld?to=friend&amp;format=html</tt>
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            HTML template: 
           <tt>/&lt;contextPath&gt;/&lt;servicePath&gt;/sample/helloworld.html?to=friend</tt>
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            XML template: 
           <tt>/&lt;contextPath&gt;/&lt;servicePath&gt;/sample/helloworld?to=friend&amp;format=xml</tt>
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            XML template: 
           <tt>/&lt;contextPath&gt;/&lt;servicePath&gt;/sample/helloworld.xml?to=friend</tt>
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <h2>Response Status</h2>
         <br>
         <p>Web Scripts use HTTP response status codes to:<br></p>
         <br>
         <ul>
          <li> inform a client of an error situation (for example, item not found)<br></li>
          <li> inform a client of an occurrence of an event (for example, item created)<br></li>
          <li> instruct a client to perform a follow-up request (for example, authorization required)<br></li>
          <li> inform a client of success<br></li>
         </ul>
         <p>Response status codes are set in the controller script via the <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23status" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">status</a> root object.<br></p>
         <p>We can add a status to our Hello World example indicating that we can only greet one person at a time i.e. the 'to' argument is specified only once. We can use status code 400 (Bad Request) to represent this. The controller script is extended as follows:<br></p>
         <pre><strong>if (argsM.to&nbsp;!= null &amp;&amp; argsM.to.length &gt; 1)<br>{<br>&nbsp;&nbsp; status.code = 400;<br>&nbsp;&nbsp; status.message = 'Can only greet one person at a time.';<br>&nbsp;&nbsp; status.redirect = true;<br>}<br>else<br>{</strong><br>&nbsp;&nbsp; model.toWho = (args.to&nbsp;!= null)&nbsp;? args.to&nbsp;: person.properties.userName; <br><strong>}</strong><br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>Redirect allows the rendering of a custom response template for the specified status code. If redirect is not set (that is, false), the response header status code is set but the relevant standard web script response template is used, as would normally apply.<br></p>
         <p>If redirect is true, then an appropriate status response template is searched for. The search is performed in the following order:<br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            Web Script specific template named 
           <tt>&lt;scriptid&gt;.&lt;method&gt;.&lt;format&gt;.&lt;code&gt;.ftl</tt>&nbsp;: located in the same folder as the web script description document and used for the specified status code only, for example 
           <br> 
           <tt>/org/alfresco/sample/helloworld.get.html.400.ftl</tt>
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            Web Script specific template named 
           <tt>&lt;scriptid&gt;.&lt;method&gt;.&lt;format&gt;.status.ftl</tt>&nbsp;: located in the same folder as the web script description document used for any status code, for example
           <br>
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <p><tt>/org/alfresco/sample/helloworld.get.html.status.ftl</tt><br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            Package level template named 
           <tt>&lt;format&gt;.&lt;code&gt;.ftl</tt>&nbsp;: this template is first located in the package of the web script, but if not found, is searched for in the parent package hierarchy, up to the root package, for example 
           <br> 
           <tt>/org/alfresco/sample/html.400.ftl</tt>
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            Package level template named 
           <tt>&lt;format&gt;.status.ftl</tt>&nbsp;: this template is first located in the package of the web script, but if not found, is searched for in the parent package hierarchy, up to the root package, for example 
           <br> 
           <tt>/org/alfresco/sample/html.status.ftl</tt>
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            Default template named 
           <tt>&lt;code&gt;.ftl</tt>&nbsp;: located in the root package and always renders html, for example 
           <br> 
           <tt>/400.ftl</tt>
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            Default template named 
           <tt>status.ftl</tt>&nbsp;: located in the root package (provided out-of-the-box) and always renders html, for example 
           <br> 
           <tt>/status.ftl</tt>
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <p>Status Response templates have access to the same root objects as standard Web Script response templates. The exception is that the default templates <tt>/&lt;code&gt;.ftl</tt> and <tt>/status.ftl</tt> only have access to the root objects '<a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23url" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">url</a>', '<a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23status" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">status</a>', '<a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23server" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">server</a>' and 'date'.<br></p>
         <p>To provide a custom Bad Request status response for our Hello World example we create the following file in the same folder as the web script description document<br></p>
         <pre>helloworld.get.html.400.ftl<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>whose content is<br></p>
         <pre><br>&nbsp;&nbsp; <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; ${status.message}<br>&nbsp;&nbsp; <br> <br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>We can also provide a meaningful response for machine-readable XML requests:<br></p>
         <pre>helloworld.get.atom.400.ftl<br></pre>
         <br>
         <pre>&lt;response&gt;<br>&nbsp; &lt;code&gt;${status.code}&lt;/code&gt;<br>&nbsp; &lt;codeName&gt;${status.codeName}&lt;/codeName&gt;<br>&nbsp; &lt;codeDescription&gt;${status.codeDescription}&lt;/codeDescription&gt;<br>&nbsp; &lt;message&gt;${status.message}&lt;/message&gt;<br>&lt;/response&gt;<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>Remember, these templates are optional, as the search for an appropriate status template will always eventually find the default template <tt>/status.ftl</tt>.<br></p>
         <br>
         <h1>Advanced Implementations</h1>
         <br>
         <h2>Configuration</h2>
         <br>
         <p>Configuration is accessed via the <tt>config</tt> root object, which is available during both controller script and template execution.<br></p>
         <p>There are 3 types of configuration, 'script', 'scoped' and 'global'. Script configuration is defined in an XML document with an arbitary structure stored locally with the Web Script. Global and scoped configuration are specified in Alfresco configuration files, as used in Alfresco Explorer.<br></p>
         <br>
         <h3>Web Script Configuration</h3>
         <br>
         <p>Web Script configuration is read from an XML file packaged with the Web Script.<br></p>
         <p>For our example Hello World service we create the following file in the same folder as the Web Script description document<br></p>
         <pre>helloworld.get.config.xml<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>Again, naming conventions apply where configuration file names have the following structure<br></p>
         <pre>&lt;serviceId&gt;.&lt;httpMethod&gt;.config.xml<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>The content of the configuration may be any valid XML.<br></p>
         <pre>&lt;helloworld&gt;<br>&nbsp; &lt;greeting&gt;hello&lt;/greeting&gt;<br>&nbsp; &lt;fromproperty&gt;userName&lt;/fromproperty&gt;<br>&lt;/helloworld&gt;<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p><span>Within a Controller Script, access to the configuration is via E4X which is essentially 'ECMAScript For XML' (tutorials can be found at </span><a class="jive-link-external-small" href="http://www.w3schools.com/xml/xml_e4x.asp" rel="nofollow">http://www.w3schools.com/xml/xml_e4x.asp</a><span> and/or </span><a class="jive-link-external-small" href="http://wso2.org/library/1050" rel="nofollow">http://wso2.org/library/1050</a><span>, </span><a class="jive-link-external-small" href="http://phpforms.net/tutorial/tutorial.html" rel="nofollow">http://phpforms.net/tutorial/tutorial.html</a><span>).</span><br></p>
         <p>We can update our Hello World Controller script example to determine how to display 'who' the greeting is from.<br></p>
         <pre>model.toWho = (args.to&nbsp;!= null)&nbsp;? args.to&nbsp;: person.properties.userName;<br><strong>var s = new XML(config.script);</strong><br>model.fromWho = person.properties[<strong>s.fromproperty</strong>]; <br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>FreeMarker has <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.freemarker.org%2Fdocs%2Fxgui.html" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">builtin support for processing XML data</a> allowing response templates direct access to configuration too. We can update our Hello World template example to extract the greeting from the configuration.<br></p>
         <pre><br>&nbsp;&nbsp; <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; At ${date?datetime}, ${fromWho?html} says ${'''config.script.helloworld.greeting'''?html} to ${toWho?html}<br>&nbsp;&nbsp; <br> <br></pre>
         <br>
         <h3>Global and Scoped Config</h3>
         <br>
         <p>Global and scoped config is read by the Alfresco <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FConfig_Service" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Configuration Service</a>. By default the following files are read:<br></p>
         <p style="min-height: 8pt; padding: 0px;">&nbsp;</p>
         <dl>
          <br>
          <dt>
           Versions 4.x:
           <br>
          </dt>
          <dd>
           <br>
           <br>
           <ul>
            <li> classpath:alfresco/web-scripts-config.xml (already exists in 'alfresco.jar'; don't overwrite it!)<br></li>
            <li> classpath:alfresco/web-scripts-cmis-config.xml<br></li>
            <li> classpath:alfresco/extension/web-api-config-custom.xml<br></li>
            <li> classpath:alfresco/extension/web-scripts-config-custom.xml<br></li>
            <li> classpath:alfresco/extension/web-scripts-cmis-config.xml<br></li>
           </ul>
           <p></p>
          </dd>
          <dt>
           Versions 5.x:
           <br>
          </dt>
          <dd>
           <br>
          </dd>
          <p></p>
          <br>
          <ul>
           <li> classpath:alfresco/web-scripts-config.xml (already exists in 'alfresco.jar'; don't overwrite it!)<br></li>
           <li> classpath:alfresco/extension/web-scripts-config-custom.xml<br></li>
          </ul>
          <p style="min-height: 8pt; padding: 0px;">&nbsp;</p>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <p>Configuration sections that do not have an evaluator or condition are known as 'global' config sections i.e. these will always appear in a configuration lookup, a typical global configuration section has the following appearance.<br></p>
         <pre>&lt;alfresco-config&gt;<br>&nbsp; &lt;config&gt;<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &lt;server&gt;<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &lt;errorpage&gt;/jsp/error.jsp&lt;/errorpage&gt;<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &lt;loginpage&gt;/jsp/login.jsp&lt;/loginpage&gt;<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &lt;guesthome enabled='true'&gt;/jsp/guesthome.jsp&lt;/guesthome&gt;<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &lt;url&gt;/&lt;/url&gt;<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &lt;url&gt;/alf&lt;/url&gt;<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &lt;url&gt;/alfresco&lt;/url&gt;<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &lt;/server&gt;<br>&nbsp; &lt;/config&gt;<br>&lt;/alfresco-config&gt;<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>Scoped configuration, on the other hand, is a configuration section that does have an evaluator and condition, for example.<br></p>
         <pre>&lt;alfresco-config&gt;<br>&nbsp; &lt;config evaluator='string-compare' condition='Remote'&gt;<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &lt;remote&gt;<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &lt;endpoint&gt;http://localhost:8080/alfresco&lt;/endpoint&gt;<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &lt;/remote&gt;<br>&nbsp; &lt;/config&gt;<br>&lt;/alfresco-config&gt;<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>For changes in these files to take effect, the ALFRESCO server must be stopped and restarted (refreshing the webscripts is not sufficient).<br></p>
         <br>
         <h3>Accessing Global and Scoped Configuration</h3>
         <br>
         <p>Accessing the configuration above is achieved using the same techniques and syntax as any other model data, the global configuration is exposed via the <tt>config.global</tt> root object and the scoped config is exposed via the <tt>config.scoped</tt> root object.<br></p>
         <p>For example to access the server configuration from the example above the following syntax would be used in a JavaScript:<br></p>
         <pre>var serverCfg = config.global.server;<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>and the following syntax would be used in a FreeMarker template:<br></p>
         <pre>&lt;serviceId&gt;.&lt;httpMethod&gt;.properties<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>Each line of the file represents a message identified by a unique key. The key may be dot separated.<br></p>
         <p>Our example consists of:<br></p>
         <pre>at=At<br>says=says<br>to=to<br>greeting.hello=hello<br>greeting.howdy=howdy<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>Messages are accessed via the template method <tt>msg</tt>.<br></p>
         <p>The Hello World HTML template is updated as follows:<br></p>
         <pre><br>&nbsp;&nbsp; <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; ${msg('at')} ${date?datetime}, ${fromWho?html} ${msg('says')} ${msg('greeting.' + config.script.helloworld.greeting)} ${msg('to')} ${toWho?html}<br>&nbsp;&nbsp; <br> <br></pre>
         <br>
         <h2>Multi-part Form Processing</h2>
         <br>
         <p>When posting a request of mimetype <tt>multipart/form-data</tt> the following additional root object is available to the Controller Script.<br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt> 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23formdata" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">formdata</a>: provides access to multipart/form-data requests allowing the upload of files.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <p>This root object allows a Web Script to read all fields included in the form including those of type 'file'. It provides a mechanism for iterating through each field and examining its meta-data such as name, value, content type etc.<br></p>
         <p>All fields that are not of type 'file' are also mapped into the <tt>args</tt> and <tt>argsM</tt> root objects allowing access to fields by name.<br></p>
         <p>View the <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts_Examples%23File_Upload" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">File Upload Example</a> to see how <tt>formdata</tt> is used to upload files into the Alfresco Repository. <br></p>
         <br>
         <h2>Request Processing</h2>
         <br>
         <p>A Controller Script can gain access to a request body allowing the processing of content posted to a Web Script.<br></p>
         <p>By default, the following root object is provided:<br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            requestbody: a 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F4.0_JavaScript_API%23ScriptContent_API" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">ScriptContent</a> representing the content of the request body
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <p>As with <tt><a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23formdata" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">formdata</a></tt>, the content may be converted to a string (if plausible) or written to an output stream such as a content object held in the Alfresco Repository.<br></p>
         <p>Often, content is posted in a structured form such as XML or JSON. In these cases, the content can be converted to a string and subsequently parsed by the controller script. However, this can become cumbersome or error prone if the parsing is required by several Web Scripts implementations. To alleviate this problem, the <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Web Scripts framework</a> provides the notion of a <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework%23Format_Reader_SPI" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Format Reader</a> which parses a request of a given mimetype into an object structure that is then automatically provided to the Controller Script.&nbsp; <br></p>
         <p>Out-of-the-box, the Web Script framework provides the following Format Readers.<br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            JSON: parses a request of mimetype 
           <tt>application/json</tt> into a JSON object named 
           <tt>json</tt>
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            Atom Feed: parses a request of mimetype 
           <tt>application/atom+xml;type=feed</tt> into an 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fincubator.apache.org%2Fabdera%2Fdocs%2Fapi%2Forg%2Fapache%2Fabdera%2Fmodel%2FFeed.html" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Apache Abdera Feed</a> object named 
           <tt>feed</tt>
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            Atom Entry: parses a request of mimetype 
           <tt>application/atom+xml;type=entry</tt> into an 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fincubator.apache.org%2Fabdera%2Fdocs%2Fapi%2Forg%2Fapache%2Fabdera%2Fmodel%2FEntry.html" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Apache Abdera Entry</a> object named 
           <tt>entry</tt>
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            Atom&nbsp;: parses a request of mimetype 
           <tt>application/atom+xml</tt> into either an Abdera Feed or Entry object named 
           <tt>feed</tt> and 
           <tt>entry</tt> respectively
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <p>Format Readers are not invoked automatically i.e. sending a JSON request to a Web Script does not automatically provide a <tt>json</tt> root object to the Controller Script. The fall-back <tt>requestbody</tt> is provided instead.<br></p>
         <p>To explicitly initiate a Format Reader requires a Controller Script whose name is structured:<br></p>
         <pre>&lt;serviceId&gt;.&lt;httpMethod&gt;.&lt;format&gt;.js<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>e.g.<br></p>
         <pre>folder.post.json.js&nbsp; =&gt; create 'json' root object for Controller Script when <tt>application/json</tt> mimetype is posted<br>folder.post.atomentry.js&nbsp; =&gt; create 'entry' root object for Controller Script when <tt>application/atom+xml;type=entry</tt> mimetype is posted<br></pre>
         <br>
         <h2>Runtime Cache Controls</h2>
         <br>
         <p>Runtime cache control is optionally specified via the root object <tt><a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23cache" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">cache</a></tt> which is available to the Web Script Controller script. At runtime, expiry criteria may be set, and <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Advanced_Description_Options" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">definition-time controls</a> may be overridden.<br></p>
         <br>
         <h1>Java-Backed Implementations</h1>
         <br>
         <p>Sometimes, scripts and templates are not powerful enough to implement the required functionality behind a URI.&nbsp; For example, streaming content.<br></p>
         <p>For these scenarios it is possible to bind an Alfresco Spring configured Java Bean into the Web Script. The Java Bean may take full control, or work in conjunction with the script and templates.<br></p>
         <p>For reference, you may browse these <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FJava-backed_Web_Scripts_Samples" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Java samples</a>.<br></p>
         <br>
         <h2>Spring Bean Declaration</h2>
         <br>
         <p>To bind a Spring bean to a Web Script it is only necessary to create a bean with an id of the following structure:<br></p>
         <pre>id='webscript.&lt;packageId&gt;.&lt;serviceId&gt;.&lt;httpMethod&gt;'<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>and ensure its parent is the 'webscript' bean:<br></p>
         <pre>parent='webscript'<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p><strong>Note:</strong> &lt;packageId&gt; is the package (directory) that the Web Script descriptor (.desc.xml file) is located in, <em><strong>not</strong></em> the package of the Java class that implements the logic for the Web Script.<br></p>
         <p>For example:<br></p>
         <pre>&lt;bean id='<strong>webscript.org.alfresco.sample.helloworld.get</strong>'<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; class='my.java.package.structure.HelloWorld'<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; parent='<strong>webscript</strong>' /&gt;<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>Note that the bean id is made up of:<br></p>
         <br>
         <ul>
          <li> prefix = webscript <em>(must always start with this value)</em><br></li>
          <li> packageId = org.alfresco.sample<br></li>
          <li> serviceId = helloworld<br></li>
          <li> httpMethod = get<br></li>
         </ul>
         <p>From this we can determine that the descriptor for this Web Script is called helloworld.get.desc.xml and is located in the directory org/alfresco/sample (either in the repository or in the classpath, as described in <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Deciding_Where_to_Place_Web_Script_Implementation" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Deciding Where to place Web Script Implementation</a>).<br></p>
         <p>As with any Spring bean, other service(s) your Java class requires (including the Alfresco APIs) may be dependency injected into your Java bean.<br></p>
         <br>
         <h2>Web Script Java Class</h2>
         <br>
         <p>The Java Class must implement the Java Interface:<br></p>
         <pre>org.alfresco.web.scripts.WebScript<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>which declares the following methods:<br></p>
         <pre>/**<br> * Gets the Service Description<br> * <br> * @return service description<br> */<br>public WebScriptDescription getDescription();<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <br>/**<br> * Execute service<br> * <br> * @param req<br> * @param res<br> * @throws IOException<br> */<br>public void execute(WebScriptRequest req, WebScriptResponse res)<br>&nbsp; throws IOException;<br></pre>
         <br>
         <h2>Java Helper Classes</h2>
         <br>
         <p>Abstract helper classes are also provided to simplify the development of a Java backed Web Script.<br></p>
         <p>The first helper class is:<br></p>
         <pre>org.alfresco.web.scripts.AbstractWebScript<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>which allows a Web Script to take full control over the request. This is achieved by providing an implementation of the <tt>execute</tt> method. The helper class provides access to information such as the Web Script description document and methods for invoking JavaScript and templates.<br></p>
         <p>The second helper class is:<br></p>
         <pre>org.alfresco.web.scripts.DeclarativeWebScript<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>which allows a web script to mix Java, JavaScript, and templates. This kind of Web Script supports all the behaviour described in this document, with the addition of first executing some Java. As with the controller script, the Java code can build a data model that is available to Response templates. The Java to be executed is placed into the <tt>executeImpl</tt> method.<br></p>
         <br>
         <h2>Managing Response Status</h2>
         <br>
         <p>A Java implemented web script also has support for response status codes. There are two approaches to sending a response code:<br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            Approach 1 - Throw an Exception
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <p>All exceptions thrown from a Web Script are caught by the Web Script Runtime and converted to response status codes. By default, the status code 500 (Internal Error) is used. However, the exception <tt>WebScriptException</tt> supports the constructor:<br></p>
         <pre>public WebScriptException(int statusCode, String message)<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>This constructor is used to explicitly set a response code in an error situation, for example<br></p>
         <pre>if (req.getParameter('q') == null || req.getParameter('q').length() == 0)<br>{ <br>&nbsp;&nbsp; throw new WebScriptException(HttpServletResponse.SC_BAD_REQUEST, 'Search term not provided');<br>}<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>Using this approach will always render the relevant status response template.<br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            Approach 2 - Explicit Setting of Response Status
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <p>The helper class <tt>DeclarativeWebScript</tt> provides the method executeImpl whose signature is:<br></p>
         <pre>protected Map&lt;String, Object&gt; executeImpl(WebScriptRequest req, WebScriptStatus status, Cache cache)<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>The status argument may be used to explicitly set a response status code &amp; message, as well as control the redirect to a status response template, for example<br></p>
         <pre>if (req.getParameter('q') == null || req.getParameter('q').length() == 0)<br>{<br>&nbsp;&nbsp; status.setCode(HttpServletResponse.SC_BAD_REQUEST);<br>&nbsp;&nbsp; status.setMessage('Search term not provided');<br>&nbsp;&nbsp; status.setRedirect(true);<br>&nbsp;&nbsp; return;<br>}<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>Exceptions may be handled as follows:<br></p>
         <pre>catch(AuthenticationException e)<br>{<br>&nbsp;&nbsp; status.setCode(HttpServletReponse.SC_FORBIDDEN);<br>&nbsp;&nbsp; status.setMessage('Invalid username &amp; password');<br>&nbsp;&nbsp; status.setException(e);<br>&nbsp;&nbsp; status.setRedirect(true);<br>}<br></pre>
         <br>
         <h2>Creating a New Kind of Web Script</h2>
         <br>
         <p>By default, Alfresco Web Scripts support an <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework%23Web_Script_MVC" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">MVC style</a> of implementation. Sometimes, it's useful to override the default behavior to add an extra capability, or provide a completely different style of Web Script such as those that need to stream large amounts of data back on the response. This can be done by developing a Java-backed implementation, however, it cannot be re-used across several Web Scripts without changes to Spring configuration.<br></p>
         <p>A Web Script 'Kind' allows a Java-backed implementation to be named, and for any Web Script Description Document to state it wants to use that implementation instead of the out-of-the-box one provided by Alfresco. See list of currently available <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Kinds" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Web Script kinds</a>.<br></p>
         <p>The steps for creating a new 'Kind' are:<br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            Implement a Web Script backing bean
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <p>The steps here are exactly the same as for any other Java-backed implementation as described above.<br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            (optional) Implement a Description Document Extension
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <p>The backing bean may be configured via extensions to the Web Script Description Document. To access those extensions it is necessary to provide an implementation of the interface:<br></p>
         <pre>org.alfresco.web.scripts.DescriptionExtension<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>which defines the following method:<br></p>
         <pre>/**<br> * Gets the custom description extensions<br> * <br> * @param serviceDescPath&nbsp; path to service doc<br> * @param serviceDesc&nbsp; service doc input stream<br> * @return&nbsp; extensions mapped by name<br> */<br>public Map&lt;String, Serializable&gt; parseExtensions(String serviceDescPath, InputStream servicedesc);<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>The method parses the complete Description Document (XML), extracts its extensions and places them into a map (indexed by the name of extension) which is returned. It is called when the Web Script is registered with the Web Script framework.<br></p>
         <p>Spring is used to register the Description Extension implementation:<br></p>
         <pre>&lt;bean id='<strong>webscriptdesc</strong>.my.kind.of.web.script' class='my.kind.of.WebScriptDocumentExtension'/&gt;<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>The id is the same as the Web Script backing bean except it starts with <tt>webscriptdesc</tt> instead of <tt>webscript</tt>.<br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            (optional) Access Extensions within your Web Script Implementation
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <p>To gain access to your extension values within your backing bean you can use the following method which returns the map created above:<br></p>
         <pre>getDescription().getExtensions()<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>That's it. To use your new 'Kind' of Web Script refer to <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Advanced_Description_Options" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Advanced Description Options</a>. Note: The id referenced in the <tt>kind</tt> attribute is specified without the <tt>webscript.</tt> prefix.<br></p>
         <br>
         <h1>How Do I Administer Web Scripts?</h1>
         <br>
         <h2>Resetting the Web Script Index</h2>
         <br>
         <p>New and updated Web Scripts can be registered without restarting the Alfresco server. This makes it easy to use the Alfresco Repository to develop Web Scripts.<br></p>
         <p>To register a Web Script:<br></p>
         <br>
         <ol>
          <li> Visit the index page as described in <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Listing_Available_Web_Scripts" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Listing Available Web Scripts</a>.<br></li>
          <li> Click on <strong>Refresh</strong> to re-register all Web Scripts.&nbsp; <br></li>
         </ol>
         <h2>Logging</h2>
         <br>
         <p>The <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">3.0 Web Scripts Framework</a> provides <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework%23Logging" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">logging</a> of Web Script registration and execution.<br></p>
         <br>
         <h2>Testing</h2>
         <br>
         <p>Various <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Testing" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">tools</a> are available for testing Web Scripts.<br></p>
         <br>
         <h2>Dump &amp; Load</h2>
         <br>
         <p>Web Scripts that are not Java-backed may be exported from one Repository and imported to another via the simple <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Script_Dump_and_Load" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Web Script Dump and Load</a> utility.<br></p>
         <p>The utility is also useful for viewing the complete implementation of a Web Script in a single page, allowing it to be copied and sent via e-mail or posted to the forums for sharing or diagnosing a problem.<br></p>
         <br>
         <h2>Localization of Status Code Messages</h2>
         <br>
         <p>The resource bundle <tt>/alfresco/messages/webscripts.properties</tt> contains status code names and descriptions for all HTTP codes.<br></p>
         <br>
         <h1>Web Script Framework</h1>
         <br>
         <p>Learn more about<br></p>
         <br>
         <ul>
          <li> <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework%23Web_Script_MVC" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Web Script MVC</a><br></li>
          <li> <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework%23Configuration" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Configuration of the framework</a><br></li>
          <li> <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework%23Architecture" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Design of the framework</a><br></li>
          <li> <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework%23Available_Runtimes" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Runtimes</a>, <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework%23Available_Authenticators" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Authenticators</a> and <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework%23Available_Containers" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Containers</a><br></li>
          <li> <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F3.0_Web_Scripts_Framework%23Extending_the_Framework_%28SPIs%29" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Extending the Framework</a><br></li>
         </ul>
         <h1>Appendix A: Web Script Root Objects</h1>
         <br>
         <h2>formdata</h2>
         <br>
         <p>A host object providing access to multipart/form-data requests allowing file upload from a web script. See <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts_Examples%23File_Upload" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">example</a>.<br></p>
         <p>Note: You <strong>must</strong> use enctype='multipart/form-data' in your form tag or the formdata variable will not be populated with fields.<br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            hasField: boolean indicating the existence of a named form field in the multipart request
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            fields: an array of 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23formfield" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">formfield</a> where each entry represents a field within the multipart request
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <h3>formfield</h3>
         <br>
         <p>A host object providing access to a form field within a multipart/form-data request.<br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            name: the name of the form field (Note that form fields may not be uniquely named)
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            isFile: boolean indicating whether this field represents a file (content)
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            value: string representing the field value (in the case of isFile is true, the filename will be returned, use 
           <em>content</em> instead)
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            content: a 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FJavaScript_API%23ScriptContent_API" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">ScriptContent</a> representing the content of the field
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            mimetype: the mimetype of the content (or null, if isFile is false)
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            filename: the filename of the source file used to provide the content (or null, if isFile is false, or a filename was not provided)
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <h2>url</h2>
         <br>
         <p>A host object providing access to the URL (or parts of the URL) that triggered the web script.<br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            context: Alfresco context path, for example 
           <tt>/alfresco</tt>
           <br>
          </dt>
          <dt>
            serviceContext: Alfresco service context path, for example 
           <tt>/alfresco/service</tt>
           <br>
          </dt>
          <dt>
            service: Web script path, for example 
           <tt>/alfresco/service/blog/search</tt>
           <br>
          </dt>
          <dt>
            full: Web script URL, for example 
           <tt>/alfresco/service/blog/search?q=tutorial</tt>
           <br>
          </dt>
          <dt>
            templateArgs: a map of substituted token values (within the URI path) indexed by token name
           <br>
          </dt>
          <dt>
            args: Web script URL arguments, for example 
           <tt>q=tutorial</tt>
           <br>
          </dt>
          <dt>
            match: The part of the web script URL that matched the web script URL template
           <br>
          </dt>
          <dt>
            extension: The part of the web script URL that extends beyond the match path (if there is no extension, an empty string is returned)
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <p><br><br>For example, imagine a web script URL template of<br></p>
         <pre>/user/{userid}<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>and a web script request URL of<br></p>
         <pre>/alfresco/service/user/fred?profile=full&amp;format=html<br></pre>
         <br>
         <p>The <tt>url</tt> root object will respond as follows:<br></p>
         <br>
         <ul>
          <li> <tt>url.context</tt> =&gt; /alfresco<br></li>
          <li> <tt>url.serviceContext</tt> =&gt; /alfresco/service<br></li>
          <li> <tt>url.service</tt> =&gt; /alfresco/service/user/fred<br></li>
          <li> <tt>url.full</tt> =&gt; /alfresco/service/user/fred?profile=full&amp;format=html<br></li>
          <li> <tt>url.args</tt> =&gt; profile=full&amp;format=html<br></li>
          <li> <tt>url.templateArgs['userid']</tt> =&gt; fred<br></li>
          <li> <tt>url.match</tt> =&gt; /user/<br></li>
          <li> <tt>url.extension</tt> =&gt; fred<br></li>
         </ul>
         <h3>URL and authentication</h3>
         <br>
         <p>You can reuse the web clients authentication by using the /alfresco/wcservice/ URL to reference you web script. Change the URL to /alfresco/service/ and you will get an HTTP authentication prompt even if you are logged in in the Alfresco web client. The first option is the most convenient for the end user, the second may be useful while testing with different accounts.<br></p>
         <br>
         <h2>status</h2>
         <br>
         <p>An associative array of response status properties that allow control over the status and content of the Web Script response.<br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            code: (read/write) status code (primarily a HTTP status code, but can be any number)
           <br>
          </dt>
          <dt>
            codeName: (read) human readable status code name
           <br>
          </dt>
          <dt>
            codeDescription: (read) human readable status code description
           <br>
          </dt>
          <dt>
            message: (read/write) status message
           <br>
          </dt>
          <dt>
            redirect: (read/write) a boolean indicating whether to redirect to a status specific response template
           <br>
          </dt>
          <dt>
            exception: (read/write) the exception (if any) which has caused this status
           <br>
          </dt>
          <dt>
            location: (read/write) the absolute URI to which the client should resubmit a request - often used with 3xx redirect status codes.&nbsp; See 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts_Examples%233xx_Status_Code_Redirection" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">example</a>.
           <br>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <br>
         <h2>cache</h2>
         <br>
         <p>An associative array of cache control properties that allow control over how the Web Script response is cached. See <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2FWeb_Scripts_Examples%23Cache" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">example</a>.<br></p>
         <br>
         <dl>
          <dt>
            neverCache: (read/write boolean) control whether Web Script response should be cached at all; 
           <tt>true</tt> means never cache. If not set, the default value is specified by the 
           <a class="jive-link-external-small" href="https://community.alfresco.com/external-link.jspa?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwikitest.alfresco.com%2Fwiki%2F%23Caching" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">cache control</a> section of the Web Script definition.
           <br>
          </dt>
          <dt>
            isPublic: (read/write boolean) control whether web script response should be cached by public caches. If not set, the default value is specified by the
